10 min
Seller's Claim to a Child Born Within Six Months: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Ruling on seller's paternity claim with proof and Shafi'i objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a seller claims a child born within six months of the sale and explain the Quranic proof for the minimum pregnancy period.

Core Idea
The child belongs to the seller if born within six months; the mother becomes umm walad and the sale is void.

This lesson examines a scenario from Hanafi fiqh on sale (buyu'): when a slave-girl is sold and gives birth within six months, the seller's claim of paternity is accepted. The ruling hinges on the minimum duration of pregnancy being six months, derived from Quranic verses. The passage also presents the Shafi'i objection, making this a classic inter-madhhab dispute. Understanding this ruling requires tracing the legal inference (istidlal) from the Quran and applying the concept of umm walad.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the ruling
Identify the key elements: a seller sells a slave-girl, she gives birth within six months, and the seller claims the child. The Hanafi ruling: the child is attributed to the seller, the mother becomes umm walad, and the sale is rescinded with the price returned.
The time threshold (within six months of sale) is crucial.
2
Identify the legal consequences
The mother attains the status of umm walad (she becomes free upon the seller's death and cannot be sold). The sale becomes void (fasid) because selling an umm walad is not permissible.
This consequence directly follows from the established lineage.
3
Trace the proof from Quran and Companions
The author combines two verses: Al-Baqarah 2:233 (breastfeeding two complete years) and Al-Ahqaf 46:15 (gestation and weaning thirty months). Subtracting 24 months from 30 leaves 6 months as the minimum pregnancy. The incident of Umar and Ali confirms that a woman giving birth at six months is not punished for zina.
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof) with qati' thubut but zanni dalalah (interpretive certainty).
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The proof works by arithmetic: thirty months total minus twenty-four months of maximum breastfeeding equals six months minimum gestation. The incident of Umar and Ali applies this principle to avoid a hadd punishment.
The method is istidlal by combining revealed texts, not direct prescription.
5
Contrast the Shafi'i objection and note the thamarah al-khilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that selling the slave-girl implies an admission that she was not pregnant at the time of sale, so the seller's later claim is contradictory and not accepted. The Hanafi school allows the claim because the textual proof overrides the inference from the sale. The practical difference: Hanafi school voids the sale and establishes lineage; Shafi'i school upholds the sale and does not attribute the child to the seller.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different weighting of textual and contextual evidence.

(75) And if a man sells a slave-girl, then she comes with a child, and the seller claims it: if she gives birth within less than six months from the day he sold her, then the child is the son of the seller, and its mother is the umm walad of the seller, and the sale is rescinded and the price is returned. Explanation: If a man sold his slave-girl, then she gave birth within six months of sale, the seller claims the child, the child becomes the seller's, the mother becomes his umm walad, the sale is voided, and the seller must return the price to the buyer. The minimum pregnancy period is six months because that is the shortest duration of pregnancy. The proof is the narration: Umar was brought a woman who gave birth after six months and wanted to stone her, but Ali said there is no stoning; Umar asked Ali, and he recited: 'Mothers shall breastfeed their children for two complete years... and his gestation and weaning are thirty months' (al-Baqarah 2:233, al-Ahqaf 46:15). So six months is the gestation period, and two years complete the breastfeeding; therefore, no hadd on her. Then Imam al-Shafi'i says: The seller's claim is not accepted because selling is an admission that at the time of sale there was no pregnancy in the slave-girl's womb. Therefore, claiming the child now is contradictory.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the claim of paternity when a sold slave-girl gives birth shortly after the sale. The author first states the ruling: if the birth occurs within six months of the sale and the seller claims the child, the child is attributed to the seller, the mother becomes his umm walad (a status that frees her upon his death and prohibits her sale), and the sale is rescinded with the price returned. The reason is that the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months, as established by combining Quranic verses: the total period of gestation and weaning is thirty months, and maximum weaning is two years (24 months), leaving six months as the minimum gestation. The author supports this with a historical incident involving Umar and Ali, where a woman who gave birth at six months was not punished for zina. This proof is presented as the dalil for the Hanafi position. The passage then notes a disagreement from Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that the act of selling the slave-girl is an implicit admission that she was not pregnant at the time of sale; therefore, the seller's later claim should not be accepted. The Hanafi response is not explicitly given here, but the implication is that the clear textual evidence from the Quran and the practice of the Companions takes precedence over the logical inference from the sale. The commentary on the Urdu side further clarifies the reasoning and the legal consequences.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master; upon the master's acknowledgment, she becomes free upon his death and cannot be sold.
الدعوى (al-da'wa): A legal claim, specifically here the seller's assertion of paternity over the child born to the sold slave-girl.

Priority of Seller's Claim Over Buyer's for a Child Born Within Six Months
Ruling that seller's claim takes precedence when child born within six months of sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when both the seller and buyer claim a child born within six months of sale and explain the rationale based on the presumption of conception timing.

Core Idea
The seller's claim to a child born within six months of sale is preferred because conception likely occurred under his ownership.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi law of claims (da'wa) regarding a slave-child born shortly after a sale. Both parties may claim the child, but the timing of birth provides a clue. The passage establishes a clear rule based on probability and the presumption of continuity (istishab).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
Both the seller and the buyer claim the child born to a slave-girl after her sale. The child's birth occurs within six months of the sale.
The six-month period is critical.
2
Apply the six-month rule
Since the child is born within six months of the sale, conception must have occurred before the sale, i.e., during the seller's ownership.
The minimum gestation period is six months in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Determine the likelihood of conception
Because the buyer could have had intercourse only after purchase, the short interval makes it improbable that the child is from the buyer.
This is based on probability, not certainty.
4
State the ruling
The seller's claim is given precedence (awla) over the buyer's claim.
The ruling is clear: دعوة البائع اولی.
5
Understand the legal principle
The ruling is rooted in istishab (presumption of continuity) and the principle that the more probable claim is given priority.
This is a practical application of qarina (circumstantial evidence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۲۸۰۵] (۷۶) وان ادعاه المشترى مع دعوة البائع او بعدها فدعوة البائع اولی. اگر بچے کا دعوی مشتری نے کیا بائع کے دعوی کے ساتھ یا بائع کے دعوی کے بعد تو بائع کا دعوی اولی ہے۔ بائع کے دعوی کے بعد یا بائع کے دعوی کے ساتھ مشتری نے بھی دعوی کیا کہ یہ بچہ میرا ہے۔ پھر بھی بائع کے دعوی کو ترجیح دی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ جس وقت حمل ٹھہرا اسی وقت سے بائع کا دعوی منسوب ہے اور مشتری کا دعوی خریدنے کے بعد شمار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ خریدنے کے بعد باندی سے جماع کر سکتا ہے اور یہاں چھ ماہ کے اندر اندر بچہ دیا ہے اس لئے اندازہ یہ ہے کہ خریدنے سے پہلے حمل ٹھہرا ہے اس لئے غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ بائع کا علوق ہے اس لئے اسی کے دعوی کو تر جیح ہوگی۔
(76) And if the buyer claims it along with the seller's claim or after it, then the seller's claim is more deserving. Explanation: If the buyer claims the child along with the seller's claim or after it, the seller's claim is given precedence. Because at the time of conception, the claim relates to the seller, while the buyer's claim relates to after the purchase. The buyer could have intercourse after purchase, but since the child was born within six months, it is likely that conception occurred before the purchase, so the seller's claim is given priority.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage address a scenario where both the seller and the buyer claim the child born within six months of the sale. The ruling states that the seller's claim takes precedence over the buyer's, whether the buyer claims simultaneously with the seller or after. The reasoning provided in the Urdu commentary is that the timing of conception (within six months of sale) indicates that the slave-girl was already pregnant when sold. Therefore, the child is more likely the seller's. The buyer could have had intercourse after purchase, but the short interval makes it improbable that the child is from the buyer. This is based on a presumption of continuity (istishab) of the pregnancy from the seller's period of ownership.

Key Terms
اولی (awla): More deserving, taking precedence; used to indicate that the seller's claim is given priority over the buyer's.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the buyer did not purchase the child
D) Because the seller has witnesses

Key Takeaway
The seller's claim to a child born within six months of sale is given priority because probability and istishab indicate conception during his ownership.

Seller's Claim Rejected When Birth After Six Months
States ruling on seller's paternity claim for births after six months.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a seller's paternity claim for a child born between six months and two years after the sale and identify the condition under which the claim is accepted.

Core Idea
A seller's claim of paternity is rejected unless the buyer confirms—uncertainty defeats the claim.

In the previous lesson, we learned that if a slave-girl gives birth within six months of purchase, the seller's claim of paternity is accepted without question. But what if the birth happens after six months? The possibility that the buyer could have fathered the child introduces uncertainty. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on that scenario and the one condition that can salvage the seller's claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time window
The ruling applies when the child is born after more than six months but less than two years from the date of sale. Note that 'more than six months' means any time after the six-month mark, not at six months exactly.
Six months is the minimum pregnancy duration in Hanafi law; any birth within six months is attributed to the seller.
2
State the default ruling
The seller's claim that the child is his is not accepted by default. The child is not attributed to him, and he cannot, for example, reclaim the slave-girl as an umm walad unless the claim is accepted.
The passage says لم تقبل دعوة البائع فيه – 'the seller's claim in it is not accepted'.
3
Analyze the rationale
After six months, the buyer could have had intercourse with the slave-girl and fathered the child. Since there is no certainty that the child was conceived before the sale, the seller's claim is weak and thus rejected.
The Urdu commentary explains: ہوسکتا ہے کہ خریدنے کے بعد مشتری نے باندی سے وطی کی ہو – the buyer may have had intercourse after purchase.
4
Identify the condition for acceptance
The only way the seller's claim is accepted is if the buyer explicitly confirms (tasdiq) that the child belongs to the seller. This is voluntary; the buyer cannot be forced to confirm.
تصدیق (tasdiq) means confirmation; the buyer acknowledges the child is from the seller.
5
Determine the effect of confirmation
Once the buyer confirms, the child's lineage is established with the seller, and all legal consequences follow (e.g., the child becomes free, inherits, and the slave-girl may become an umm walad if she had not already).
The Urdu commentary states: بچے کا نسب بالغ سے ثابت ہوگا – the child's lineage is proven from the seller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۰۶ (۷۷) وان جائت به لاكثر من ستة اشهر ولا قل من سنتين لم تقبل دعوة البائع فيه الا ان يصدقه المشترى. اگر بچہ جنی چھ مہینے سے زیادہ میں اور دو سال سے کم میں تو بائع کا دعوی قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا مگر یہ کہ مشتری اس کی تصدیق کرے۔ خرید نے کے چھ مہینے کے بعد باندی نے بچہ دیا اور دو سال سے پہلے، اب بائع دعوی کرتا ہے کہ یہ بچہ میرا ہے تو بائع کی بات نہیں مانی جائے گی۔ ہاں مشتری اس کی تصدیق کرے کہ بچہ بائع ہی کا ہے تو بائع کی بات مان لی جائے گی اور بچے کا نسب بالغ سے ثابت ہوگا۔ چھ مہینے کے بعد پیدا ہوا تو کوئی ضروری نہیں ہے کہ بائع کا ہی علوق ہو، ہوسکتا ہے کہ خریدنے کے بعد مشتری نے باندی سے وطی کی ہو اور اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا ہو۔ اس لئے بائع کا بچہ ہونا کوئی یقینی بات نہیں ہے۔ البتہ مشتری تصدیق کر دے کہ بائع کا ہی ہے تو بچہ بائع کا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ مشتری کے تصدیق کے بعد کوئی معارض نہیں رہا۔
(77) And if she gives birth after more than six months and less than two years, the seller's claim in it is not accepted unless the buyer confirms him. Explanation: If the slave-girl gives birth more than six months after the purchase but before two years, the seller's claim is not accepted unless the buyer verifies it. After six months, it is not necessary that the child is from the seller; the buyer could have had intercourse after purchase and the child could be from him. So the seller's claim is not certain. However, if the buyer confirms that the child is the seller's, then the child's lineage is established with the seller because no one else contests.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage deals with the seller's claim when the birth occurs after six months from the sale but within two years. The ruling is that the seller's claim is not accepted on its own because the child could have been conceived after the sale (by the buyer). The minimum pregnancy period (six months) has passed, so the birth does not necessarily point to pre-sale conception. However, if the buyer voluntarily confirms that the child is the seller's, then the claim is accepted and the child's lineage is established. This is because the buyer's confirmation removes any contradiction, and no one else has a competing claim. The Urdu commentary explains that after six months, it is possible for the buyer to have fathered the child, so the seller's claim is not automatically accepted.

Key Terms
تصدیق (tasdiq): Confirmation by the buyer that the child belongs to the seller, which makes the seller's claim accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
A seller's paternity claim for a child born after six months from the sale is rejected unless the buyer voluntarily confirms the child is the seller's.

Claim After Child's Death: No Nasab or Umm Walad
Ruling on claim after child's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a seller's claim of paternity after the child's death and identify the condition that must be met for the claim to be accepted.

Core Idea
A claim of parentage must be made while the child is alive; after death, it is too late.

In Hanafi sales law, a seller may claim that a child born to a purchased slave woman is his own, which establishes lineage and makes the mother an umm walad. However, this claim must be made during the child's lifetime. This lesson examines a key passage from the matn that clarifies the ruling when the child dies before any claim is made.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
The passage describes a sale where the purchased slave woman gives birth within six months. The seller then claims the child is his, but only after the child has died. Identify the parties and the timing.
2
Extract the ruling
The text states: 'the lineage in the child is not established nor the umm walad status in her.' This is the clear legal outcome.
3
Recognize the implicit condition
The ruling implies that a claim made during the child's lifetime would have been accepted, but after death it is not. The condition for acceptance is that the child must be alive at the time of the claim.
4
Understand the rationale
The Urdu commentary explains that establishing lineage is meant to avoid the child being labeled illegitimate (walad al-zina). Since the child is dead, this purpose no longer applies; the claim cannot retroactively benefit a deceased child.
5
Apply the ruling to similar cases
Consider if the child died but the seller made the claim before death (even if not yet pronounced): the claim would be accepted. The key is the timing relative to the child's death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۲۸۰۷ (۷۸) وان مات الولد فادعاه البائع وقد جائت به لاقل من ستة اشهر لم يثبت النسب في الولد ولا الاستيلاد في. بچے کی زندگی میں بائع نے اپنی اولاد ہونے کا دعوی نہیں کیا، بچہ مرگیا اس کے بعد لڑکا ہونے کا دعوی کیا تو بائع سے بچے کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہو گا اور نہ اس کی ماں ام ولد بنے گی۔ بچے کا نسب ثابت کرنا ایک مجبوری ہے کیونکہ کسی سے بچے کا نسب ثابت نہیں کیا جائے گا تو بچہ حرامی ہوگا جو جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے جیسے ہی
(78) And if the child dies, and the seller claims it even though she gave birth within less than six months, the lineage in the child is not established nor the umm walad status in her. Explanation: If the seller did not claim the child during its lifetime but claims after its death, the child's lineage is not established with the seller, and the mother does not become umm walad. Establishing lineage is a necessity because otherwise the child would be considered illegitimate, which is not permissible. Therefore, as soon as...
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage covers the situation where the child dies before the seller makes a claim. Even if the birth was within six months (which would otherwise support the seller's claim), the claim after death is not accepted for establishing lineage or umm walad status. The rationale from the Urdu commentary is that the purpose of establishing lineage is to avoid labeling the child as illegitimate (walad al-zina). Once the child has died without a claim during its lifetime, the need to avoid illegitimacy no longer exists for the child itself. Although the text is cut off, the clear ruling is that neither the child's lineage to the seller nor the mother's status as umm walad is established. This prevents the mother from gaining freedom or inheritance rights through that status.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity; establishment of father-child relationship.
استیلاد (istilad): The status of a slave woman becoming umm walad by bearing her master's child.

B) Neither the child's lineage nor the mother's umm walad status is established
C) The seller can still claim and all effects apply
D) The mother automatically becomes umm walad

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a seller's claim of paternity to establish nasab and umm walad status is only valid if made during the child's lifetime; after death, the claim is rejected.

Imprisonment of a Solvent Debtor: Conditions and Procedure
Sets procedure for imprisoning a debtor only after order and proof of default

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three-step procedure for imprisoning a debtor in Hanafi fiqh and apply the hadith evidence to determine when imprisonment is permissible.

Core Idea
Imprisonment is for the solvent procrastinator, not for the debt itself.

This lesson examines the precise procedure a judge must follow before imprisoning a debtor. The Hanafi school emphasizes caution: imprisonment is not a first resort but a punishment for deliberate default after proof of ability to pay. We will analyse the textual evidence and the conditions that must be satisfied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three-step judicial process
The passage describes that after debt is proven and creditor demands imprisonment, the judge must (1) not hasten to imprison, (2) order the debtor to pay, and (3) only imprison if the debtor refuses. Identify each step in the source text.
The order is mandatory: proof → demand → order → refusal → imprisonment.
2
Specify the type of debt subject to imprisonment
The text restricts imprisonment to debts 'in exchange for which property came into his hand,' such as sale price or loan repayment. Determine what types of debts are included and which are not.
This excludes debts arising from torts or non-property obligations.
3
Extract the hadith evidence and its legal implication
The author cites the hadith: 'The solvent one who delays makes his honour and punishment permissible.' Explain how this hadith justifies imprisonment as a ta'zir penalty for procrastination (matl), not for inability to pay.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala) according to the author.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf reportedly held that imprisonment is not allowed for debts of food or similar items. Compare this with the general ruling in the text and understand its practical effect.
The majority (including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) applies the general ruling; Abu Yusuf's view is a minority exception.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a case where a debtor has money but refuses to repay a loan, walk through the judge's steps and determine whether imprisonment is permissible.
Ensure all prerequisites are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا ثبت الحق عنده وطلب صاحب الحق حبس غريمه لم يعجل بحبسه وامره بدفع ما عليه فان امتنع حبسه في كل [۲۹۰۴] (۱۷) جب ان کے نزدیک حق ثابت ہو جائے اور حق والا قرض خواہ کو قید کرنے کا مطالبہ کرے تو اس کو قید کرنے میں جلدی نہ کرے۔ اور اس کو حکم دے ادا کرنے کا جو اس پر ہے۔ پس اگر وہ ادا کرنے سے باز رہے تو اس کو ہر اس قرض میں قید کرے جس کے بدلے میں اس کے ہاتھ میں مال آیا ہو۔ مثلا بیع کا شمن اور قرض کا بدل۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمر بن الشريد عن ابيه عن رسول الله الله قال: لى الواجد يحل عرضه وعقوبته، قال ابن المبارك يحل عرضه يغلظ له وعقوبته يحبس له (ب) دوسری رویت میں ہے۔ عن بهر بن حكيم عن ابيه عن جده ان النبي الا الله حبس رجلا في تهمته (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الدین هل تحبس به ، ج ۲، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۳۶۳۰/۳۶۲۸ / بخاری شریف، باب لصاحب الحق مقال ، ص ۳۲۳، نمبر ۲۴۰۱، کتاب ا؛ استقراض رالنسائی شریف، باب مطل الغنی ص ۶۴۵ نمبر ۴۶۹۳)
When the right is established with him and the claimant asks to imprison his debtor, he should not hasten to imprison him, but order him to pay what is due. Then if he refuses, he may imprison him in every [debt] in exchange for which property came into his hand, such as the price of a sale or the return of a loan. The evidence is the hadith from 'Amr ibn al-Sharid from his father from the Messenger of Allah: 'The solvent one who delays payment makes his honour and punishment permissible.' Ibn al-Mubarak said: 'His honour is permissible means to be severe with him, and his punishment means to imprison him.' In another narration from Bahz ibn Hakim from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet imprisoned a man on suspicion. (Abu Dawud, Bukhari, Nasa'i)
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the judge's procedure in debt cases. When a debt is proven (e.g., by confession) and the creditor demands imprisonment of the debtor, the judge must not immediately imprison. First, he orders the debtor to pay. If the debtor refuses without valid excuse and defaults, then the judge may imprison him for debts that involve exchange of property, such as sale price or loan repayment. The proof is the hadith that a solvent person who delays payment makes his honour and punishment permissible, and the practice of the Prophet in imprisoning for suspicion. In the Hanafi school, this imprisonment is a ta'zir punishment for delay, not for the debt itself.

Key Terms
غريم (gharim): Debtor or the one against whom debt is established
مطل (matl): Procrastination or delay in payment despite being solvent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what type of debt qualifies for imprisonment when the debtor refuses to pay?
A) Any debt proven in court.
B) Debts that are in exchange for property, such as sale price or loan repayment.
C) Only debts of food and necessities.
D) Debts incurred from torts or damages.

Key Takeaway
Imprisonment of a debtor in Hanafi fiqh is a ta'zir punishment only for a solvent person who refuses to pay after being ordered by the judge, and only for debts involving exchange of property.

Division of Real Estate on Purchase Claim
Ruling on dividing real estate on purchase claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing real estate when claimants allege purchase and explain why no evidence is required.

Core Idea
A purchase claim among living co-owners is accepted without evidence due to Muslim probity and absence of a deceased.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hanafi fiqh: when several people claim that they jointly purchased a piece of real estate, the judge (qadi) may divide it among them immediately, without demanding any further proof. The reasoning is distinct from inheritance cases, where evidence is required to protect the rights of the deceased and potential unknown heirs. Here, the claim is made by living parties against themselves, and the principle of Muslim probity (al-salamah) applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the passage carefully. Note that the claimants are living people who assert that they bought the real estate jointly. The claim is not against a deceased person, and no other heirs are involved.
Contrast with inheritance disputes where the deceased's rights and potential unknown heirs require evidence.
2
Apply the Principle of Muslim Probity
The Hanafi school presumes that a Muslim is truthful (al-asl al-salamah). Since the claimants are Muslims, their statement is accepted as sufficient proof in this context.
This principle is derived from the hadith: 'The Muslims are just witnesses over each other.'
3
Note the Absence of Third-Party Harm
There is no judgment against a deceased person (who cannot defend themselves) and no risk of a hidden heir appearing. Therefore, the judge can divide without evidence.
If there were a deceased or potential heir, evidence would be required to safeguard their rights.
4
State the Ruling
Based on the above, the judge divides the real estate among the claimants immediately, without requiring witnesses or documents.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ادعوا في العقار انهم اشتروه قسمه بینهم . کچھ آدمی قاضی کے سامنے دعوی کرتے ہیں کہ یہ زمین ہے جس کو ہم لوگوں نے خریدی ہے تو بغیر کسی مزید بینہ کے قاضی ان کے درمیان تقسیم کر دے۔ یہاں میت کے خلاف فیصلہ نہیں ہے اور نہ مزید کسی وارث کے ظاہر ہونے کا خدشہ ہے۔ اور ظاہر یہی ہے کہ ان لوگوں نے خریدی ہے اس لئے ان کے درمیان تقسیم کر دے۔
If they claim regarding real estate that they bought it, he divides it among them. Some people claim before the judge: This land we have purchased. So without any further evidence, the judge divides it among them. Here there is no judgment against the deceased and no fear of another heir appearing. And it is apparent that they bought it, so he divides among them.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage provides a separate ruling: if claimants (co-owners) assert that they jointly purchased the real estate, rather than inherited it, the judge can divide it immediately without any evidence. The reasoning differs from the inheritance cases: there is no deceased person involved, so no judgment against the deceased, and no risk of an unknown heir appearing. The purchase claim is about themselves, and as Muslims, they are presumed truthful. Therefore, division is straightforward.

Key Terms
اشتروه (ishtarawhu): They bought it (past tense).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, when claimants say they bought real estate, why does the judge not require evidence?
A) Because real estate is durable and can always be recovered.
B) Because there is no deceased person involved, so no judgment against the deceased.
C) Because they must have a sale deed and the judge presumes it existed.
D) Because the judge already knows the property was sold.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a purchase claim among living co-owners is accepted without evidence due to Muslim probity and the absence of a deceased party.

10 min
Division of Purchased Property in the Absence of a Co-Owner
Ruling on division of jointly purchased property when one co-owner is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the judge must not divide jointly purchased property when one co-owner is absent, and explain the three reasons and the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Division of purchased property cannot proceed without all co-owners present, as it risks injustice and is effectively a judgment absent the person.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Samari clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi law: inherited property may be divided even if an heir is absent due to the risk of loss, but purchased property is different. The author presents three reasons and a Quranic proof to establish that the judge must wait until the absent co-owner returns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the division (qismah) of jointly purchased property by the judge. The ruling is that it is not permissible (haram) to do so when one co-owner is absent.
This applies only to purchased property, not inherited property.
2
Understand the exception for inheritance
In inheritance, division is urgent because heirs may neglect the property. The author contrasts this with purchase, where owners are vigilant.
Thus the rule differs based on the source of ownership.
3
Analyze the three reasons
The first reason: no urgency because buyers care for their property. Second: the absent co-owner may have invested more, and present ones could cheat. Third: dividing in absence would be judgment against an absent person (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib), which is prohibited.
Each reason reinforces the prohibition.
4
Recognize the Quranic proof
The author cites verse 4:58, which commands delivering trusts and judging with justice. This implies that one cannot judge against an absent person, and the absent's share is a trust that must be protected.
The dalil is from the Quran, categorically transmitted but its implication is derived by reasoning.
5
Apply the rule
If two of three co-purchasers ask the judge to divide, the judge must refuse until the third returns. The absent person may send an agent, but cannot be forced.
The ruling ensures fairness and prevents potential injustice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۵۰] (۱۹) اور اگر وہ خریدنے والے تھے تو ان میں سے ایک کی غیر حاضری میں تقسیم نہیں کی جائے گی۔ مثلا تین آدمیوں نے مل کر ایک گھر خریدا۔ پھر دو آدمی ملکر قاضی کے پاس آئے کہ مجھے تقسیم کر کے دیں۔ اور ایک خریدار غائب ہے تو قاضی گھر تقسیم نہ کرے۔
وراثت کی شکل میں مال میت کا تھا جب تک تقسیم کر کے نہ دیں، وارثین اس کی حفاظت میں لا پرواہی کریں گے اس لئے اس کو جلدی تقسیم کرکے دینا ضروری ہے۔ اور خریدے ہوئے مال کی ضیاع کا خریدار کو فکر ہے اس لئے اس کو جلدی تقسیم کرنا ضروری نہیں جب تک کہ غائب نہ آجائے (۲) غائب کا اپنا لگایا ہوا مال ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ممکن ہے کہ اس سے زیادہ حصہ لگایا ہو اور حاضرین چکما دے کر زیادہ لے لینا چاہتا ہو اس لئے غائب کی حاضری کے بعد پتا چلے گا کہ اس کا حصہ کتنا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی حاضری کے بغیر تقسیم نہ کرے (۳) یہ نکتہ بھی ہے کہ مورث دنیا سے جا چکا ہے اس لئے وارث اس کی جانب سے خصم ہوں گے اس لئے قضا علی الغائب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور خریدنے کی شکل میں غائب آدمی دنیا حاشیہ : ( الف ) اللہ تعالی تم کو حکم دیتے ہیں کہ امانت والے کو امانت پہنچاؤ، اور جب تم لوگوں کے درمیان فیصلہ کرو تو انصاف کے ساتھ فیصلہ کرو۔ اللہ تعالی تمہیں اچھی نصیحت کرتے ہیں۔ میں موجود ہے اس لئے اس کی جگہ کوئی خصم نہیں بن سکے گا۔ اس لئے اس کی غیوبت میں فیصلہ کریں تو قضا علی الغائب ہوگا جو جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہاں ایک آدمی بھی غائب ہو تو تقسیم نہیں کی جائے گی۔
[2950] (19) And if they were buyers, then division will not be made in the absence of one of them. For example, three men jointly purchased a house. Then two men came to the judge asking to divide it, and one buyer is absent, so the judge will not divide the house. In the case of inheritance, the property belonged to the deceased; until division is made, the heirs may be negligent in its preservation, so it is necessary to divide quickly. But for purchased property, the buyer is concerned about its loss, so quick division is not necessary until the absent one comes. (2) It is the absent one's own property he invested; so it is possible that he invested more share, and the present ones may deceive to take more, so it will be known after the absent one's presence how much his share is. Therefore do not divide without his presence. (3) Also, the deceased has passed away from the world, so the heirs are opponents on his behalf, so there is no judgment against an absent person. But in the case of purchase, the absent person exists in the world, so no one can be his opponent. Therefore if they decide in his absence, it would be judgment against an absent person, which is not permissible. Therefore, if even one person is absent, division will not be made.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that when jointly owned property is purchased (not inherited), division cannot take place if one co-owner is absent. The author gives three reasons: (1) In inheritance, heirs may waste the property, so quick division is necessary; but buyers care for their property, so delay is not harmful. (2) In purchase, each partner has invested his own money, and the absent one may have invested a larger share; present ones might cheat by taking more, so waiting for the absent one reveals the true shares. (3) In inheritance, the deceased is no longer alive, so the heirs represent him as opponents, thus no judgment is passed against an absent person. But in purchase, the absent person is alive, so any decision would be against an absent person, which is not allowed. The proof for the general principle of appointing an agent for the absent one is the Quranic verse (4:58) commanding trusteeship and just judgment.

Key Terms
قسمت (qismah): Division of jointly owned property into separate shares.
غائب (gha'ib): A person who is absent from the location where the division is requested.
قضا علی الغائب (qada' 'ala al-gha'ib): A legal judgment passed against a person who is not present to defend himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is division of inherited property considered more urgent than division of purchased property?
A) Because inherited property is less valuable.
B) Because heirs may neglect and waste the property.
C) Because the deceased's debts must be paid quickly.
D) Because the judge has authority over inheritance only.

Key Takeaway
When property is purchased jointly, the judge must not divide it in the absence of any co-owner due to the risk of injustice and the prohibition of judgment against an absent person.

Dividing Mixed Properties: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
States the ruling on dividing mixed properties and the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reason for the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions on dividing mixed properties, and apply the correct method based on the co-owners' circumstances.

Core Idea
Different genera must be divided separately unless all co-owners agree or the qadi deems combination more beneficial.

When co-owners hold shares in multiple properties of different types—like a house and a plot of land—how should the division be carried out? Should each property be split independently, or can they be pooled and divided as a whole? This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students on this question, and the practical implications for partition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed issue
The act is the division of jointly owned properties of different genera (e.g., house and land). The issue is whether each property must be divided separately among all co-owners, or whether mixing and dividing them together is permitted.
The dispute is about the method of partition, not its permissibility.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that each genus must be divided separately. For example, if there is a house and land, both the house and the land must each be divided among all co-owners. They cannot be assigned to individuals unless all co-owners agree.
His proof is the hadith of the Prophet equating ten sheep to one camel in division.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani allow mixing the properties and dividing them as a whole if that is more beneficial. The qadi has discretion to choose the method that is most equitable, even if some co-owners object.
They focus on the overall benefit (maslaha) of the co-owners.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, each partner gets a share in both properties (e.g., 50% of the house and 50% of the land). Under Sahibayn, the qadi could assign the entire house to one partner and the entire land to the other, with a monetary adjustment to equalize values.
The difference affects convenience and transaction costs.
5
Apply the ruling in a simple scenario
Two partners own a house worth 10,000 and land worth 5,000. Under Abu Hanifa, each gets a 50% share in both. Under Sahibayn, the qadi might give the house to one and land to the other, with a payment of 2,500 from the house-taker to the land-taker.
The cash adjustment compensates for the value difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كتاب القسمة
واحد قسمت كل دار على حدتها في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا رحمهما الله تعالى ان كان الاصلح لهم قسمة بعضها في بعض قسمها [ ۲۹۵۴ (۲۳) وان كانت دار وضيعة او داروحانوت قسم كل واحدة على حدته [۲۹۵۵] (۲۴) وينبغي للقاسم ان يصوّر ہے۔ اور اس کے خلاف ہو تو مکان کی قیمت گھٹ جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے ظاہری برابری کے علاوہ باطنی خوبیوں کو بھی ملحوظ رکھا جائے گا۔ اور اس کے اعتبار سے قیمت لگے گی۔ اصول حضرت امام اعظم کے نزدیک باطنی خوبیوں کو بھی ملحوظ رکھا جائے گا، ہاں! تینوں حصے دار ایک ایک مکان لینے پر راضی ہو تو اس طرح بھی تقسیم کر دے۔
صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کو قاضی کی رائے پر چھوڑ دے۔ اگر ان کے لئے یہی مناسب ہو کہ تینوں کو ایک ایک مکان دیدے اور اوپر سے کوئی رقم نہ دے تو قاضی کو اس کا بھی اختیار ہے چاہے حصہ دار اس پر راضی نہ ہوں۔ اور اس کا بھی اختیار ہے کہ ہر ہر مکان میں تینوں کا حصہ ڈالے، پھر ہر مکان کی قیمت لگا کر توافق کرے۔
اصول صاحبین کے نزدیک ظاہری برابری کو لحوظ رکھا جائے گا باطنی خوبیوں کی طرف زیادہ توجہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔
[ ۲۹۵۴] (۲۳) اگر مکان اور زمین ہوں یا مکان اور دکان ہوں تو ہر ایک کو علیحد علیحدہ تقسیم کرے۔
مثلا دو حصے دار ہیں اور مالیت میں ایک مکان اور زمین ہے۔ تو مکان میں بھی دونوں کو حصہ دیں اور زمین میں بھی دونوں کو حصہ دیں۔
ہاں ! اگر ایک آدمی صرف مکان لینے پر اور دوسرا آدمی صرف زمین لینے پر راضی ہو جائے تو ٹھیک ہے۔
مکان الگ جنس ہے اور زمین الگ جنس ہے اور دونوں کی قیمتوں میں بہت فرق ہوتا ہے اس لئے بالا تفاق مکان میں بھی دونوں کا حصہ ہوگا اور زمین میں بھی دونوں کا حصہ ہوگا۔ اور یہ گویا کہ تبدیل اور خرید ہوگی۔ اس لئے دونوں کی قیمت لگا کر تو افق کیا جائے گا۔ مثلا مکان کی قیمت دس ہزار ہے اور زمین کی قیمت پانچ ہزار ہے۔ تو مکان لینے والے پر زمین لینے والے کو ڈھائی ہزار دینا ہو گا ۔ یہی حال مکان اور دکان کا ہے کہ دونوں دو جنس ہیں۔ عن عباية بن رفاعة بن رافع بن خديج عن جده قال كنا مع النبي الله بذي الحليفة ... ثم قسم فعدل عشرة من الغنم ببعير (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب قسمته الغنم ص ۱۳۳۸، نمبر ۲۴۸۸) اس حدیث میں بکری الگ جنس ہے اور اونٹ الگ جنس ہے اس لئے دس بکریوں کو ایک اونٹ کے برابر کیا۔ پس کسی کو ایک اونٹ دیا تو اس سے توافق کرنے کے لئے دوسرے کو دس بکریاں دی۔ اسی طرح مکان اور دکان کا حال ہو گا۔
The commentary says: Regarding the division of a house and land or a house and shop, Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: each is divided separately. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: if it is more beneficial for them, they may be divided together. If it is otherwise, the price of the property decreases. Therefore, besides apparent equality, inner qualities should also be considered, and valuation should be based on that. According to Imam A'zam, inner qualities are considered. Yes, if the three partners agree to take one house each, then division can be done that way. The two companions say: leave it to the qadi's opinion. If it is more appropriate to give each of the three a house without any additional payment, the qadi has that authority even if the partners do not agree. He also has the authority to include all three shares in each house and then assess the value of each house and reconcile. According to the two companions, apparent equality is observed, and inner qualities are not given much attention. [2954] (23) If there is a house and land, or a house and a shop, each is divided separately. For example, there are two partners and they have a house and land. Then both should get a share in the house and both in the land. Yes, if one person agrees to take only the house and the other only the land, that is fine. The house is a separate genus and the land is a separate genus, and their values differ greatly. Therefore, by agreement, both will have a share in the house and both in the land. This is like exchange and purchase. Hence, the values of both are assessed and reconciliation is done. For example, the house is worth ten thousand and the land is worth five thousand. Then the one taking the house must give two and a half thousand to the one taking the land. The same applies to a house and a shop: they are two different genera. The hadith: from 'Abaya bin Rifa'a bin Rafi' bin Khadij from his grandfather, he said: 'We were with the Prophet (peace be upon him) at Dhul-Hulaifa... then he divided and made ten sheep equivalent to one camel' (Bukhari, chapter on division of sheep, p. 1338, no. 2488). In this hadith, the goat is a separate genus and the camel is a separate genus, so ten goats were equated to one camel. Thus, if someone was given a camel, then to reconcile, the other was given ten goats. Similarly is the case of a house and a shop.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage presents the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions on the division of mixed properties (house and land, house and shop). It is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa holds that each property should be divided separately among all co-owners, because they are different genera. The two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, allow mixing the properties and dividing them in a way that may be more beneficial, leaving the method to the qadi's discretion. The commentary gives examples and a hadith proof: the Prophet equated ten sheep to one camel in division, showing that different genera are valued separately. According to the text, the default is separate division unless all partners agree otherwise.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners.
جنس (jins): Genus or category of property; here meaning different types like house vs. land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how should a house and a shop be divided among co-owners?
A) They are combined into one division.
B) Each is divided separately among all co-owners.
C) The qadi decides arbitrarily.
D) They are sold and the proceeds divided.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, default division of mixed properties is per genus, but the qadi may combine them for benefit, following the Sahibayn's view.

Procedure for the Qasim: Mapping, Measuring, Valuing, and Drawing Lots
Describes the recommended procedure for dividing property among co-owners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended steps for a qasim in dividing property and explain the purpose of each step.

Core Idea
The qasim must ensure each share is independent and assigned by lottery to prevent accusations of favoritism.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari outlines the recommended procedure for a qasim appointed to divide joint property. The steps ensure transparency and impartiality, grounded in the Prophetic practice of drawing lots. Understanding this procedure is essential for those involved in inheritance or partnership divisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The qasim's division is a recommended act (mandub). The text uses 'ينبغي' (it is recommended).
2
List the procedural steps
The qasim should: 1) map the property, 2) measure land or value buildings, 3) separate each share with its path and water right, 4) number the shares, 5) draw lots to assign. The goal is to eliminate mutual dependency.
The goal is to eliminate mutual dependency.
3
Note the evidence
The hadith of Khaybar shows division into shares; the hadith of drawing lots among wives shows legitimacy. These are zanni proofs but sufficient for recommendation.
4
Understand the rationale
Lottery prevents accusations of favoritism and ensures fairness.

ما يقسمه ويعدله ويذرعه ويقوم البناء ويفرز كل نصيب عن الباقي بطريقه وشربه حتى لا يكون لنصيب بعضهم بنصيب الآخر تعلق ثم يكتب اساميهم و يجعلها قرعة [۲۹۵۶] (۲۵) ثم يلقب نصيبا بالاول والذى يليه بالثانى والذى يليه بالثالث وعلى هذا ثم يخرج نام لکھ لے اور اس کا قرعہ بنالے۔ بہت سی چیزوں کو تقسیم کرنا ہے اس لئے ان کو صحیح تقسیم کرے۔ اور سہولت ہو تو اس کے لئے یہ طریقہ بہتر ہے کہ جن چیزوں کو تقسیم کرنا ہے ان کا پورا نقشہ بنالے، زمین وغیرہ ہو تو اس کی پیمائش کرے اور ہر ٹکڑے کو برابر ناپ لے۔ عمارت ہو تو اس کی قیمت لگائے اور مکان اور زمین کے ہر حصے کو اس کے راستے اور نالی کے ساتھ الگ الگ کرے تا کہ گھر سے نکلنے میں یاز مین کو سیراب کرنے میں دوسرے سے کوئی تعلق ندر ہے اور آگے چل کر جھگڑا نہ پڑے۔ پھر ہر ایک حصے کا نام لکھ لے اور اس کا قرعہ بنالے تا کہ قرعہ ڈالنے میں آسانی ہو۔ حدیث میں ہے حضور نے خیبر کی زمین کا چھتیں سوٹکڑے فرمائے تھے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن بشير بن يسار مولى الانصار عن رجال من اصحاب النبي الا الله ان رسول الله الا الله لما ظهر على خيبر قسمها على ستة وثلاثين سهما جمع كل سهم مائة سهم الخ (الف) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب ماجاء فی حکم ارض خیبر ، ج ۲ ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۰۱۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ خیبر کی زمین کے چھتیں حصے کئے اور ہر حصے کے ساتھ ایک سو حصے تھے جس کا مجموعہ چھتیں سو حصے ہوئے۔ اور ان میں سے آدھے کو پندرہ سو مجایدین پر تقسیم فرمایا جس میں سے پیدل کو ایک حصہ اور گھوڑے سوار کو دو حصے عنایت فرمایا، مجموعہ اٹھارہ سو حصے ہوئے۔ اس سے اشارہ ملتا ہے کہ کس طرح زمین کے حصے بنائے۔
شرب : پانی جانے کی نالی، نصیب : حصہ۔
[۲۹۵۶] (۲۵) اور ایک حصے کا نام پہلے رکھے اور جو اس سے متصل ہو اس کا دوسرا اور جو اس کے متصل ہے تیسرا اسی طرح لکھتے جاؤ، پھر قرعہ نکالے، پس جس کا نام پہلے نکلے اس کے لئے پہلا حصہ اور جس کا نام دوسرے مرتبہ میں نکلے اس کے لئے دوسرا حصہ۔ جتنے حصے ہوں سب پر نمبر لگائے ایک، دو، سه، چار کر کے۔ پھر قرعہ نکالے جس کا نام پہلے نکلے اس کو پہلا حصہ دیدے۔ جس کا نام دوسری مرتبہ نکلے اس کو دوسرا حصہ دے۔ جس کا نام تیسری مرتبہ میں نکلے اس کو تیسرا حصہ دے اسی طرح کرتا چلا جائے۔ اس کے بغیر بھی کام چل سکتا ہے۔ لیکن ایسا اس لئے کرے تا کہ حصے دار یہ نہ کہے کہ قاضی نے فلاں کی طرفداری کی ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ بیوی کو سفر میں ساتھ لے جانے کے لئے قرعہ ڈالتے تھے اور جس کا نام نکلتا تھا ان کو ساتھ لے جاتے تھے۔ عن عائشة ان النبی ا كان اذا سافر اقرع بین نساى (ب) ابن ماجہ شریف، باب القضاء بالقرعة ) دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ غلام کی تقسیم قرعہ سے کی۔
حاشیه : (الف) حضور نے جب خیبر پر فتح پائی تواس کو چھتیں ٹکڑوں میں تقسیم کیا اور ہرکھڑے میں سو حصے تھے (ب) آپ جب سفر فر ماتے تو بیویوں کے درمیان قرعہ
ڈالتے۔
The commentary says: What the divider should divide: he should map it, make it equal, measure it, value the building, and separate each share from the rest with its pathway and water channel so that no share has a connection with another share. Then he writes their names and makes a lottery. [2956] (25) Then he labels the first share as first, the one next to it as second, the one next as third, and so on. Then he draws lots: whose name comes first gets the first share, whose name comes second gets the second, etc. Then he writes the names and makes a lottery. Many things are to be divided, so he should divide them correctly. For convenience, it is better to make a complete map of the things to be divided. If it is land, he should measure it and measure each piece equally. If it is a building, he should value it. He should separate each share of house and land with its pathway and water channel so that there is no dependency on others for exit or irrigation, to avoid future disputes. Then he writes the name of each share and makes a lottery for ease of drawing. The hadith: the Prophet made thirty-six portions of the land of Khaybar. The hadith: from Bashir bin Yasar, mawla of the Ansar, from men among the companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that when the Prophet conquered Khaybar, he divided it into thirty-six shares, each share comprising one hundred shares... (Abu Dawud, chapter on the ruling of the land of Khaybar, vol. 2, p. 68, no. 3012). This hadith indicates how the plots of land were made. Sharb: water channel; naseeb: share. [2956] (25) And he sets one share as first, the adjacent as second, the next as third, and so on. Then he draws lots: whose name comes first gets the first share, whose name comes second gets the second, and so on. All shares are numbered one, two, three, four. Then lots are drawn. This is done so that partners do not say that the qadi favored someone. The hadith: the Prophet used to draw lots among his wives when he wanted to travel, and he would take the one whose name came out (Ibn Majah, chapter on judgment by lottery). Another narration mentions division of slaves by lottery.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage provides practical guidelines for the qasim (divider) when dividing property among co-owners. It is a procedural ruling. The qasim should first map the property, measure it, and value any buildings. Then separate each share with its own pathway and water channel to ensure independence. After that, he writes the names of the shares and draws lots to assign them impartially. The numbering and lot-drawing prevent accusations of favoritism. The hadith of Khaybar shows that the Prophet divided land into defined shares, and the hadith of drawing lots among wives shows the legitimacy of using lottery for fair distribution. The commentary emphasizes that these steps are recommended to ensure equity and avoid disputes.

Key Terms
قرعة (qur'a): Lottery or drawing lots used to assign shares impartially.
قاسم (qasim): The person appointed to divide property among co-owners, often a qadi or his deputy.
شرب (sharb): Water channel or right of passage for irrigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the qasim draw lots after numbering the shares?
A) Because the shares are unequal.
B) To prevent partners from accusing the qadi of favoritism.
C) Because the Prophet commanded it explicitly.
D) To make the division faster.

Key Takeaway
The recommended Hanafi procedure for dividing property includes mapping, measuring, valuing, separating shares, and using a lottery to ensure impartiality.

Partition with Different Genres Requires Mutual Consent
Ruling that cash is not included in property division without mutual consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on including dirhams and dinars in partition and apply the condition of mutual consent to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Mixing different genres in partition is an exchange requiring consent; without it, the division is invalid.

When co-owners divide jointly owned property, the partition must respect each owner's share. A critical Hanafi rule distinguishes between pure division of identical items and exchanges of different types. This lesson explains why cash and real estate cannot be forced into a single division without mutual agreement, supported by hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The inclusion of dirhams/dinars (cash) in the division of other property like real estate. The ruling: such inclusion is not allowed without mutual consent of the partners.
The passage uses 'لا يُدخل' (not included) implying prohibition.
2
Understand the rationale: genre difference
The commentary explains that dirhams/dinars and real estate are different genres (jins). Therefore, including them in a single division is not pure partition (qisma) but an exchange (bay'), which requires consent.
Hanafi fiqh: partition of different types is treated as a sale.
3
Examine the example
Two partners share a house and 10,000 dirhams. Each should get half of each. If one gets more house and the other more cash, this is an exchange. Without consent, the judge cannot enforce it.
The numerical imbalance (e.g., extra house portion for extra cash) triggers sale rules.
4
Analyze the proof from the ship hadith
The hadith of Nu'man bin Bashir compares Muslims on a ship drawing lots for upper/lower parts. This indicates that when physical division is impossible, adjustment by value is permissible. Hence, in necessity, the judge may authorize compensation with consent (or by necessity).
Hadith is ahad, but used as evidence for necessity.
5
Distinguish consent vs. necessity
Normally, exchange requires consent. However, if the property cannot be physically divided equally (e.g., a single room), the judge may permit compensation with extra cash even without full consent, based on the ship hadith.
This is the exception: necessity overrides the general rule.

[۲۹۵۷] (۲۶) اور تقسیم میں داخل نہیں ہوں گے در اہم اور دینار گر حصہ داروں کی رضا مندی ہے۔ مثلا ایک مکان ہے اور دس ہزار درہم ہے اور دو حصے دار ہیں۔ اس لئے مکان میں دونوں کو آدھا آدھا حصہ ملنا چاہئے اور درہم میں بھی آدھا آدھا یعنی پانچ پانچ ہزار ملنا چاہئے۔ لیکن ایک حصے دار کو مکان میں سے آدھا سے زیادہ دیدے اور اس کے بدلے دوسرے حصے دار کو پانچ ہزار درہم کے بجائے سات ہزار درہم دیدے تا کہ یہ دو ہزار مکان کی زیادتی کے بدلے میں ہو جائے تو یہ دونوں کی رضامندی کے بغیر قاضی نہیں کر سکتا۔ ہاں دونوں اس پر راضی ہوں تو درست ہے۔
مکان الگ جنس ہے اور درہم دینا را الگ جنس ہیں۔ اس لئے مکان کے ایک حصے کے بدلے میں درہم دے یہ تبدیل اور خریدنا ہے۔ تمیز اور افراز نہیں ہے۔ اور بیج اور تبدیل کے لئے دونوں کی رضامندی چاہئے۔ اس لئے یہاں بھی دونوں کی رضامندی چاہئے (۲) دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ بعض مکان اہم ہوتا ہے اس طرح کا مکان پھر نہیں مل سکتا اس لئے جس کو مکان کا حصہ زیادہ دیا جائے گا وہ خوش ہوگا اور دوسرا افسوس کرے گا۔ اور بعض مرتبہ درہم کی اہمیت زیادہ ہوتی ہے کیونکہ اس سے فوری طور پر کچھ خرید سکتا ہے اس لئے جس کو درہم ملے گا وہ خوش ہوگا۔ اس لئے ایسی صورت حال میں تبدیل کے لئے دونوں کی رضامندی ضروری ہے۔ البتہ مکان کا بعض حصہ ایسا ہو کہ اس کو دوٹکڑوں میں تقسیم کر ہی نہیں سکتے ، لازمی طور پر ایک کو زیادہ دینا پڑ رہا ہے تو ایسی مجبوری کے درجے میں قاضی کو اختیار ہے کہ ایک کو مکان زیادہ دیدے اور اس کے بدلے میں دوسرے کو درہم یا دینار زیادہ دیدے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ سمعت النعمان بن بشير عن النبي الله قال مثل القائم على حدود الله والواقع فيها كمثل قوم استهموا على سفينة فاصاب بعضهم اعلاها وبعضهم اسفلها
(ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب بل يقرع في القسمة والاستتمام فیہ ص ۳۳۹، نمبر ۲۴۹۳) اس حدیث میں سب کو کشتی کے اوپر کے حصے نہیں دیئے اور نہ سب کو کشتی کے نیچے کے حصے دیئے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجبوری کے درجے میں تبدیل کی جاسکتی ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عمران بن حصین فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک آدمی کے چھ غلام تھے اور ان کے علاوہ کوئی مال نہیں تھا اور انہوں نے موت کے وقت ان سکھوں کو آزاد کر دیا تو حضور نے ان کا حصہ کیا اور دو کو آزاد کیا اور چار کو غلام برقرار رکھا (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جو اللہ کی حدود پر قائم ہے اور جو اللہ کی حدود میں واقع ہے ایسا ہے کہ ایک قوم نے کشتی میں قرعہ ڈالا پس بعض کو اوپر کا حصہ ملا اور بعض کو نیچے کا حصہ۔
Book of Partition: The lottery: whoever's name comes out first gets the first share, and whoever comes out second gets the second share. [2957] (26) Dirhams and dinars are not included in the division except with their mutual consent. [ 272958) Then he divided... From Imran bin Husain: a man had six slaves and no other wealth, so he freed them at his death. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ divided them, freeing two and keeping four as slaves. (Reference: Ibn Majah, Bab al-Qada' bi al-Qur'a, p.336, no. 2345/2347; Bukhari, Bab hal yuqra' fi al-qisma, p.1339, no. 2493) From this hadith it is understood that for peace of heart, names can be drawn by lottery. Section [2957] (26) And dirhams and dinars are not included in the division unless the partners consent. For example, there is a house and ten thousand dirhams, and two partners. So each should get half of the house and half of the dirhams, i.e., five thousand each. But if one partner is given more than half of the house and in exchange the other partner is given seven thousand dirhams instead of five thousand, such that the two thousand is in exchange for the extra house share, then the judge cannot do this without the consent of both. Yes, if both agree, it is valid. The house is a different genre and dirhams are a different genre. So giving dirhams in exchange for a portion of the house is exchange and purchase, not differentiation and separation. And for exchange and transformation, consent of both is required. So here too consent of both is required. (2) The second reason is that sometimes the house is important, such that this type of house cannot be found elsewhere, so the one who gets more house will be happy and the other will regret. And sometimes the importance of dirhams is greater because one can immediately buy something with them, so the one who gets dirhams will be happy. Therefore, in such a situation, consent of both is necessary for exchange. However, if a part of the house cannot be divided into two pieces, and one must necessarily be given more, then in such a case of necessity, the judge has authority to give one more house and in exchange give the other more dirhams or dinars. (2) There is an indication of this in the hadith. I heard al-Nu'man bin Bashir from the Prophet ﷺ, he said: The example of one who upholds the limits of Allah and one who falls into them is like people who drew lots on a ship; some got the upper part and some got the lower part. (Reference: Bukhari, Bab hal yuqra' fi al-qisma, p.339, no. 2493) In this hadith, not all were given the upper part of the ship, nor all the lower part, from which it is understood that in cases of necessity exchange is permissible. Footnote: (a) Hadrat Imran bin Husain said that a man had six slaves and no other wealth, and he freed them at the time of his death; so the Prophet divided them, freeing two and keeping four as slaves. (b) He said: The one who upholds the limits of Allah and the one who falls into them is like a people who cast lots in a ship; some got the upper part and some got the lower part.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on partition. The author states that dirhams and dinars (cash) are not included in the division of other properties like real estate except with mutual consent of the partners. The reason is that cash and real estate belong to different genres (jins), so including them is not pure division but an exchange (bay') that requires consent. The author supports this with two hadiths: one about the Prophet ﷺ using lottery to divide six slaves of a man who died, showing that lottery can be used for peace of heart; and another about the ship (from Nu'man bin Bashir) illustrating that in cases of necessity, exchange by value is allowed. The commentary elaborates with a concrete example: two partners share a house and ten thousand dirhams; each should get half of each. If one gets more house and the other more cash, this is an exchange and needs their agreement. Without consent, the judge cannot enforce it. However, if the house cannot be physically divided into equal shares, the judge may authorize compensation with extra cash, based on the ship hadith. The footnotes repeat the hadiths in Urdu.

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Division or partition of jointly owned property among co-owners.
تراض (taradi): Mutual consent of all partners; a necessary condition for exchanges in partition.
قرعة (qur'a): Lottery used to assign shares when rights cannot be distinguished; here used for peace of heart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are dirhams and dinars not included in the division of property without mutual consent according to this passage?
A) Because they are not divisible physically.
B) Because they are of a different genre than real estate, making it an exchange requiring consent.
C) Because the judge has no authority over cash.
D) Because the Prophet forbade mixing cash in division.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi partition law, mixing different genres of property (e.g., cash and real estate) transforms the division into an exchange, which requires mutual consent of all partners unless physical impossibility necessitates a judge-authorized adjustment.

Water Channel or Path in Another's Share After Partition
Ruling with proof on post-partition encroachment of channel/path

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling and consequence when a water channel or path falls into another's share without prior condition.

Core Idea
Without a condition, a path or channel in another's share is not permitted; the division is void if diversion is impossible.

After a property is divided among heirs, it can happen that one partner's water channel or access path ends up crossing another partner's share. The Hanafi school has a clear ruling: if the encroachment can be avoided by rerouting, the owner must do so; if not, the entire partition is rescinded. This lesson examines the legal reasoning and the proofs for this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage deals with a completed partition where one partner's maseel (water channel) or tareeq (path) lies within the other partner's property without a condition (shart) stipulating such a right.
The condition is key: without it, no implied right exists.
2
State the two possible outcomes
If the channel/path can be diverted to the owner's own share, it must be done; the owner has no right to use the other's property. If diversion is impossible, the original division is rescinded (faskh al-qisma) and a new one must be made.
The distinction depends on possibility of diversion.
3
Examine the daleel (proof)
The commentator cites the prophetic principle 'la dharar wa la dirar' (no harm) and the Quranic verse (6:136) condemning unjust divisions. The verse is used by analogy: an inequitable partition is an evil judgment.
The verse condemns the polytheists' unjust allocation; here, forcing a path/channel through another's share is similarly unjust.
4
Understand the rationale
The ruling prevents perpetual harm (dharar) to the other partner. Unless the condition was agreed upon at division, no partner has the right to encumber another's share.
The principle of 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' also applies: intention matters, and here no consent was given.
5
Apply the ruling
If a judge is presented with such a case, he must order the diversion if feasible; otherwise, he nullifies the partition and orders a new division ensuring independent access and irrigation.
This is the mufta bihi position according to later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۵۸] (۲۷) پس اگر مکان تقسیم کر دیا گیا ورثہ کے درمیان اور ان میں سے ایک کی نالی پڑ جائے دوسرے کی ملکیت میں یا راستہ ہو جائے بينهم ولاحدهم مسيل في ملك الآخر او طريق لم يشترط في القسمة فان امكن صرف الطريق والمسيل عنه فليس له ان يستطرق ويسيل في نصيب الآخر وان لم يكن فسخت القسمة تش تقسیم کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ مکان کے ساتھ نکلنے کا راستہ بھی دوسرے حصے داروں کے راستے سے بالکل جدا ہو۔ اسی طرح زمین کی تقسیم کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ پانی پلانے کی نالی دوسرے حصہ داروں سے جدا ہو۔ اور اگر مجبوری ہو تو تقسیم کے وقت ہی شرط لگا دے کہ یہ مکان والا فلاں کے راستے سے گزرے گا یا یہ زمین والا فلاں کی نالی سے پانی پلائے گا۔ تاکہ بعد میں جھگڑا نہ ہو۔ لیکن ایسی کوئی شرط نہیں لگائی پھر بھی ایک آدمی کی نالی دوسرے کے حصے سے گزر رہی ہے یا ایک آدمی کا راستہ دوسرے کے حصے میں ہو کر جاتا ہے۔ پس اگر نالی مالک زمین کے حصے سے گزرنے کا امکان ہو اور گز رسکتی ہو تو دوسرے کی زمین سے نہ گزارے بلکہ اپنے حصے میں نالی کھودے اور وہاں سے پانی پلائے ۔ اسی طرح اپنے حصے میں راستہ نکالے اور اس پر چلے تا کہ آگے چل کر جھگڑانہ پڑے۔ لیکن اگر اپنی زمین سے نالی نہ نکال سکتا ہو یا اپنے حصے میں سے راستہ نہ نکال سکتا ہوتو یہ تقسیم ٹوٹ جائے گی۔ قاسم دوبارہ اس طرح تقسیم کرے کہ اپنی زمین میں نالی اور راستہ بن سکے۔ بغیر شرط اور بغیر رضامندی کے ایک کا حصہ دوسرے میں چلا جائے اچھی بات نہیں ہے، جھگڑے کا باعث ہے (۲) لا ضرر ولا ضرار کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ اس تقسیم سے دوسرے فریق کو ہمیشہ نقصان ہوتا رہے گا (۳) آیت میں ایسی تقسیم کو برا فیصلہ کہا گیا ہے۔ آیت یہ ہے۔ وجعلوا لله مما ذرأ من الحرث والانعام نصيبا فقالوا هذا لله بزعمهم وهذا الشركائنا فما كان لشركائهم فلا يصل الى الله وما كان لله فهو يصل الى شركائهم ساء ما يحكمون (الف) ( آیت ۱۳۶، سورۃ الانعام ۶ ) اس آیت میں کفار اللہ کا حصہ بتوں کو دیتے تھے تو اللہ نے فرمایا یہ کیسا برا فیصلہ ہے۔ یہاں بھی ایک آدمی کے حصے میں دوسرے کا راستہ نکالا گیا یہ بھی فیصلہ اچھا نہیں ہے اس لئے ایسی تقسیم ٹوٹ جائے گی۔ دوبارہ ایسی تقسیم کرے کہ ایک کا راستہ یا نالی دوسرے کی زمین میں نہ ہو۔
میل : سیل سے مشتق ہے، پانی پلانے کی نالی، اسی سے ہے پسیل ، پانی ہے۔
[2958] (27) Then if the house has been divided among the heirs and one of them's water channel falls into the ownership of another, or a path becomes such, between them and one of them has a water channel in the property of another or a path not stipulated in the division, and if it is possible to divert the path and water channel away, he does not have the right to use the path and channel in the other's share, and if not, the division is rescinded. The rule of division is that the exit path of a house must be completely separate from the paths of other partners. Similarly, the rule for land division is that the irrigation channel must be separate from other partners. And if there is compulsion, then at the time of division, one should stipulate that this house owner will pass through so-and-so's path, or this land owner will irrigate from so-and-so's channel, so that there is no dispute later. But if no such condition was made, yet one person's channel passes through another's share, or one person's path goes through another's share, then if it is possible for the channel to pass through the land owner's own share and can be done, then it should not be passed through the other's land; rather, he should dig a channel in his own share and irrigate from there. Similarly, he should make a path in his own share and walk on it, so that there is no dispute later. But if he cannot dig a channel in his own land or cannot make a path in his own share, then this division will be rescinded. The partitioner should make a new division such that a channel and path can be made in one's own land. It is not good for one's share to go into another's without condition and without consent; it causes disputes. (2) It is against 'la dharar wa la dirar' (no harm and no reciprocation of harm), because this division causes continuous harm to the other party. (3) In the verse, such a division is called a bad judgment. The verse is: 'And they assign to Allah from what He has created of crops and cattle a share, then they say, 'This is for Allah,' according to their claim, 'and this is for our partners.' So what is for their partners does not reach Allah, and what is for Allah reaches their partners. Evil is what they judge.' (Surah al-An'am 6:136) In this verse, the disbelievers used to give Allah's share to idols, so Allah said what a bad judgment this is. Here too, one man's path was placed in another's share, this is also not a good judgment, so such a division is rescinded. A new division should be made so that one's path or channel is not in another's land. Maseel: derived from sayl, meaning water channel; hence it is called paseel, water.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a partition already completed where one partner's water channel (maseel) or path (tareeq) ends up in the other partner's share without prior stipulation. The ruling has two parts: if it is possible to divert the channel or path away from the other's share, the owner must do so; if it is impossible, the original partition is rescinded (faskh al-qisma) and a new one must be made. The commentary explains the general rule: each partner should have independent access and irrigation. To avoid future disputes, conditions should have been stipulated at the time of division. Without conditions, if encroachment occurs, the harmed party has no right to continue using the other's property. The reasons given: such a situation causes permanent harm, contradicting the prophetic principle 'la dharar wa la dirar', and the Quranic verse (6:136) condemns unjust judgments. The word 'maseel' is defined as a water channel, derived from 'sayl' (flow).

Key Terms
مسيل (maseel): Water channel; a path for irrigation water flow. In this context, it refers to a channel that passes through another's share.
طريق (tareeq): Path or right of way for access. In partition, each partner should have independent access.
شرط (shart): Condition stipulated at the time of division, such as a path or channel right, to prevent future disputes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if, after partition, one partner's water channel cannot be diverted from the other partner's share?
A) The partner must pay compensation for use.
B) The partner must obtain permission each time.
C) The partition is rescinded and must be redone.
D) The channel is blocked and abandoned.

Key Takeaway
A water channel or path that ends up in another's share without a condition must be diverted if possible; otherwise, the entire division is void and must be redone.

Valuation of Upper and Lower Floors in Partition
Ruling on how to value separate floors of a building in partition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for dividing a multi-story building between co-owners and explain why valuation by market value is required rather than equal physical division.

Core Idea
In partition, each floor is valued independently; fair division is by value, not by area.

When co-owners share a building with separate floors, one might assume the building should be divided equally by physical area. However, Hanafi jurisprudence requires that each floor be appraised at its market value before dividing, because the lower floor typically has greater utility and thus higher value. This lesson examines the ruling from al-Sharh al-Sameri on how to value such properties in partition proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is dividing a building with separate floors between co-owners. The ruling (hukm) is that each floor must be valued separately (قوم كل). The valuation is a procedural requirement for a fair partition.
2
Recognize the three scenarios
The matn lists three cases: lower floor alone, upper floor alone, both together. In each, the instruction is identical: value each part. This shows the rule applies universally regardless of which floors exist.
3
Understand the rationale for valuation
Lower floors (sufl) are typically more valuable due to easier access, higher utility, and potential for commercial use. Equal physical division would be inequitable. Hence, market valuation ensures each co-owner receives a share proportional to their ownership.
4
Apply the rule to a simple case
Suppose two co-owners share a two-story building. Ground floor valued at 60, upper at 40. If each owns 50%, they cannot simply take one floor each because values differ. One co-owner may take the ground floor and compensate the other with 10 units, or they may sell and split the proceeds 50/50.
If the floors are independently valued, the partition can be by physical assignment with compensation, or by sale and distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۵۹] (۲۸) واذا كان سفل لا علو له او عُلو لاسفل له او سفل له علو قوم كل
[2959] (28) And if there is a lower floor without an upper floor, or an upper floor without a lower floor, or a lower floor with an upper floor, value each [part].
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding the valuation of multi-story buildings in partition. The rule: when a building consists of separate floors (lower floor sufl, upper floor uluww), each floor is valued independently, and the partition is made based on those values. The matn gives three scenarios: lower floor without upper, upper without lower, and lower with upper. The commentary (not included in this window) would presumably explain that the upper floor is generally less valuable because the lower floor can be used for stables, shops, or entered without stairs, so valuation ensures a fair division.

Key Terms
سفل (sufl): Lower floor or ground floor of a building; considered more valuable due to easier access.
علو (uluww): Upper floor or loft; less valuable because it requires stairs and has less utility for certain purposes.
قوم (qawwam): To appraise or value; in this context, the act of determining the monetary worth of each part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How should a building with a lower floor and an upper floor be divided according to this passage?
A) The lower floor goes to one partner, the upper to the other.
B) Each floor is valued separately and division is by value.
C) The entire building is sold and the proceeds divided.
D) The building is divided equally by floor area.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi partition law, a multi-story building is not divided by area but by the independent market value of each floor to ensure equitable distribution among co-owners.
