When Kharaj Exemption Applies: Flood, Drought, and Pest
Ruling on kharaj exemption due to natural calamity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that exempt kharaj and explain the evidence from the practice of Caliph Umar and the principle of capacity.

Core Idea
Kharaj is dropped when the land cannot produce due to flood, drought, or pest.

Kharaj is a land tax imposed on conquered lands in Islamic law. The Hanafi school, drawing from the practice of Caliph Umar, ties the tax to the land's productivity. When natural calamities make cultivation impossible, the obligation of kharaj falls away. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three calamities
The matn mentions water overwhelming (flood), water being cut off (drought), and a pest destroying the crop. Each condition leads to total crop failure.
2
State the ruling
If any of these occurs, no kharaj is due. The ruling is unconditional exemption.
3
Examine the dalil
The practice of Caliph Umar and the report of Hasan al-Basri emphasize that kharaj should be within the people's capacity. This principle supports exemption when production fails.
4
Understand the qiyas
The shārih uses qiyas: the principle that kharaj is based on productivity is applied to the case of calamity. The 'illa is the inability to pay due to destruction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[13064 (85)] وان غلب على ارض الخراج الماء او انقطع عنها او اصطلم الزرع أفة فلا خراج عليهم
اگر خراجی زمین پر پانی غالب آگیا یا اس سے پانی منقطع ہو گی یا آفت نے کھیتی بر باد کر دی تو ان پر خراج نہیں ہے۔
(الف) مدینہ میں حضرت عمر کوزخم لگنے سے چند دن پہلے دیکھا کہ وہ حذیفہ بن یمان اور عثمان بن حنیف کو سامنے کھڑے ہو کر کہا تم دونوں نے کیسے کیا؟ کیا تم لوگوں کو خطرہ ہے کہ زمین پر اتنا خراج ڈالا جس کی طاقت نہ ہو؟ دونوں نے جواب دیا کہ اتنا لازم کیا جس کی ان کو طاقت ہے۔ کوئی زیادہ فرق نہیں ہے۔ فرمایا دیکھ لیں کہ اگر طاقت سے زیادہ زمین پر خراج لازم کیا ہو ! دونوں نے فرمایا نہیں، زیادہ مقرر نہیں کیا ( ب ) حضرت عثمان بن حنیف نے انگور کے ایک جریب زمین پر دس درہم مقرر کیا اور کھجور کے ایک جریب زمین پر آٹھ درہم اور ترکاری کے ایک جریب زمین پر چھ درہم اور گیہوں کے ایک جریب زمین پر چار درہم اور جو کے ایک جریب زمین پر دو در ہم مقرر کیا۔
پہلے قاعدہ گزر چکا ہے کہ پیداوار کے مطابق خراج ہوگا۔ اس قاعدے پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اگر کسی مصیبت کی وجہ سے کھیتی ہی نہیں ہو پائی تو خراج ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا سیلاب نے کھیتی برباد کر دی۔ یا بارش ہی نہیں ہوئی یا کوئی آفت آگئی جس کی وجہ سے کھیتی اجڑ گئی تو اہل خراج پر خراج نہیں ہوگا ۔۔
جب کھیتی ہی نہیں ہوئی تو خراج کہاں سے دے گا (۲) اوپر کے اثر میں تھا کہ طاقت کے مطابق خراج ہو اور یہاں آفت کی وجہ سے طاقت باقی نہیں رہی اس لئے خراج ساقط ہو جائے گا (۲) اوپر کے اثر کے علاوہ یہ اثر بھی ہے۔ قال الحسن واما اراضيهم فعليها الخراج الذي وضعه عمر بن الخطاب فان احتملوا اكثر من ذلك فلا يزاد عليهم وان عجزوا عن ذلك خفف عنهم ولا يكلفون فوق طاقتهم كما قال عمر (الف) رواه حي بن آدم فی الخراج ، ص ۳۳ نمبر ۲۸ ، اعلاء السنن ، ج ثانی عشر ص ۱۴۳۷، نمبر یحیی ، ۴۱۰۰ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اگر خراج دینے والا عاجز ہو جائے تو اس سے کم کیا جائے۔ یہاں کھیتی ہوئی ہی نہیں اس لئے اس سے خراج معاف ہو جائے گا۔
لات اصطلم : صلم سے مشتق ہے جڑ سے اکھیڑ نا کھیتی بر باد ہونا، الزرع : کھیتی۔
And if water overwhelms the kharaj land, or water is cut off from it, or a pest destroys the crop, then there is no kharaj upon them.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the exemption of kharaj when the land is damaged by natural calamities such as floods, drought, or pests. The ruling states that if the land becomes unproductive due to such causes, the kharaj is dropped. The commentary explains that this is based on the principle that kharaj is tied to the land's productivity. Since the land cannot produce, the tax is not due. Evidence is drawn from the practice of Caliph Umar, who ensured that kharaj was not imposed beyond the land's capacity. The commentary also cites an effathar from Hasan al-Basri that if the people are unable to pay, it should be reduced, further supporting the exemption when the crop is entirely destroyed.

Key Terms
اصطلم (istalama): To be destroyed or uprooted; used here to describe the complete loss of crops due to pests or disease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this ruling, what happens to kharaj if the land is flooded and no crop is harvested?
A) The kharaj is still due because the land exists.
B) The kharaj is exempted because the crop is destroyed.
C) The kharaj is halved.
D) The farmer must pay from other income.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is dropped when the land's crop is wholly destroyed by flood, drought, or pest, because the tax is based on the land's capacity to produce.

Kharaj Due When Landowner Neglects Cultivation
Ruling on kharaj when owner neglects cultivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on kharaj when the owner deliberately neglects cultivation and explain why the tax remains due.

Core Idea
Negligence does not cancel kharaj; the land's productive capacity obligates the owner.

The Hanafi school holds that kharaj is an obligation tied to the land itself, not to the actual harvest. In the previous lesson, we saw that if a natural calamity destroys the crop, the kharaj is waived. But what if the owner simply chooses not to cultivate? This lesson clarifies that the tax remains due, because the fault lies with the owner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaving land uncultivated (ta'til). The ruling is that kharaj is wajib (obligatory) upon the owner.
The matn says: 'وان عملها صاحبها فعليه الخراج' — if he neglects it, kharaj is upon him.
2
Understand the reason
The commentary explains that the owner had all means to cultivate but chose not to; thus the fault is his. The kharaj is not canceled because the land was capable of production.
The Arabic commentary uses 'غلطی خود مالک زمین کی ہے' (the fault is the owner's).
3
Compare with the exception
Contrast this with the previous ruling where a natural calamity destroyed the crop. There, the kharaj is waived because the owner was not at fault. Here, the owner's deliberate neglect makes him liable.
The key distinction is fault: calamity vs. neglect.
4
State the legal principle
Liability for kharaj is attached to the land's capacity for cultivation. The owner's negligence does not remove that liability; it is a right of the state treasury.
This principle prevents avoidance of tax by deliberate idleness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[13065 (86)] وان عملها صاحبها فعليه الخراج
اور اگر بیکار چھوڑ دیا زمین کے مالک نے تو اس پر خراج ہے۔ کھیتی کرنے کی تمام سہولتیں میسر تھیں لیکن امین کے مالک نے ستی کی وجہ سے کھیتی ہی نہیں کی تواس پر خراج ہوگا۔ جہ اس سے اس کی سستی دور ہوگی (۲) غلطی خود مالک زمین کی ہے اس لئے خراج ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
مالک زمین کی غلطی ہو تو خراج ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
ات عطل : بیکار چھوڑ دیا۔
And if its owner neglects it (leaves it uncultivated), then upon him is the kharaj.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This is a ruling stating that if the landowner deliberately leaves the land uncultivated without a valid excuse (such as natural calamity), he is still liable for the kharaj. The commentary explains that since the owner chose not to cultivate despite the means being available, he is at fault, and the kharaj remains due to discourage negligence. This contrasts with the previous ruling where the crop failure was due to an external calamity.

Key Terms
عطل (attala): To leave land uncultivated or idle deliberately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is kharaj due if the landowner chooses not to cultivate the land without any natural disaster?
A) Yes, because the land is still capable of producing.
B) No, because there is no crop.
C) Only half of the kharaj is due.
D) It depends on the decision of the Imam.

Key Takeaway
Deliberate neglect of cultivation does not cancel the obligation of kharaj; the tax remains due because the land's productive capacity is the basis of liability.

Kharaj Continues After Conversion to Islam
Ruling on kharaj upon conversion to Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kharaj when a landowner converts to Islam, identify the proof from the Companion practice, and explain why kharaj remains wajib.

Core Idea
Kharaj is a land tax, not a personal tax; conversion to Islam does not remove it.

When a non-Muslim landowner accepts Islam, one might assume all state obligations are waived. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between jizya (personal poll tax) and kharaj (land revenue). This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the practice of the early caliphs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the conversion of a kharaj-paying non-Muslim to Islam. The ruling is that kharaj continues to be collected from him 'as before' (على حاله).
The ruling is clear: kharaj does not cease upon Islam.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a qawl sahabi (statement of a Companion) from 'Umar and 'Ali: 'If he becomes Muslim and owns land, we remove the jizya from him and take its kharaj.' This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut but accepted in the school.
3
Analyze the distinction between jizya and kharaj
Jizya is a personal tax on disbelief, so it is dropped upon conversion. Kharaj is a tax on the land itself, attached to the land regardless of the owner's faith. Thus, it continues.
The illa (effective cause) for kharaj is the land's productivity, not the owner's religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[13066 (87)] و من اسلم من اهل الخراج يؤخذ منه الخراج على حاله
اگر خراج دینے والا مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس سے بدستور خراج لیا جائے گا۔
مسلمانوں پر ابتدائی طور پر خراج لازم کرنا ٹھیک نہیں ہے۔ لیکن اگر پہلے سے خراج لازم ہے اور زمین کا مالک مسلمان ہو گیا تو خراج لازم ہی رہے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن عمر و على قالا اذا اسلم وله ارض وضعنا عنه الجزية واخذنا خراجها (ب)(مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۶۵ ما قالوانی الرجل من اهل الذمة يسلم من قال يرفع عنه الجزية ، ج سادس ،ص ۴۶۷، نمبر ۳۲۹۳۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسلمان ہونے سے جزیہ تو ساقط ہو جائے گا لیکن خراج ساقط نہیں ہوگا (۳) کیونکہ جزیہ کافر کے سر پر ہے جو ذلت کی چیز ہے، اور خراج اس کی حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حسن نے فرمایا بہر حال لوگوں کی زمین پر حضرت عمر نے خراج متعین کیا۔ پس اگر اس سے زیادہ خراج برداشت کر سکتی ہو تب زیادہ نہ کیا جائے اور اگر اس کی طاقت نہ رکھتی ہو تو کم کر دیا جائے۔ اور طاقت سے زیادہ مکلف نہ بنایا جائے جیسا کے حضرت عمر نے فرمایا (ب) حضرت عمر اور حضرت علی نے فرمایا اگر زمی اسلام لائے اور اس کے پاس زمین ہو تو اس سے جزیہ ختم کر دیا جائے گا اور اس سے خراج لیا جائے گا۔
And whoever from the people of kharaj becomes Muslim, the kharaj is taken from him as before.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This ruling clarifies that when a non-Muslim landowner (dhimmi) converts to Islam, the jizya (poll tax) is dropped, but the kharaj (land tax) continues to be collected. The commentary explains that jizya is a personal tax on disbelief, whereas kharaj is a tax on the land itself, attached to the land regardless of the owner's faith. Evidence is cited from the practice of Caliphs Umar and Ali, who said: 'If he becomes Muslim and owns land, we remove the jizya but take the kharaj from him.'

Key Terms
الجزية (al-jizyah): A poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state, symbolizing protection and subordination.
الخراج (al-kharaj): A land tax imposed on agricultural land in conquered territories, regardless of the owner's faith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to kharaj when a dhimmi landowner converts to Islam?
A) Kharaj is dropped along with jizya.
B) Kharaj continues to be collected.
C) Kharaj is halved.
D) Only jizya is dropped, but kharaj is doubled.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is a land tax that continues even after the owner converts to Islam; jizya is a personal tax that is dropped upon conversion.

Muslim Buying Kharaj Land from Dhimmi
Ruling on permissibility and obligation of kharaj on purchased kharaj land.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Muslim buying kharaj land from a dhimmi and explain the legal consequence that kharaj remains obligatory on the land.

Core Idea
Buying kharaj land does not remove the kharaj; the tax obligation transfers to the Muslim buyer.

This passage addresses a critical issue in Islamic land taxation: when a Muslim purchases land that was originally subject to kharaj (land tax) from a dhimmi, does the Muslim become liable for the tax? The Hanafi school rules that the purchase is permissible but disliked, and the kharaj remains due. The author supports this with actions of the Companions and a statement of Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the basic ruling on a Muslim buying kharaj land? State the hukm level (mubah, makruh, etc.) and the consequence regarding kharaj payment.
The text clearly states 'ja'iz' (permissible) but the second athar indicates dislike.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? Identify the two athar from the Companions and their sources.
The proofs are from Sunan al-Bayhaqi, classified as ahad athar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these proofs support the ruling? Explain the legal reasoning linking the action/statement to the hukm.
The first athar shows permissibility by practice; the second shows karahah by explicit disapproval.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any disagreement within or outside the Hanafi school? Mention the potential view of absolute prohibition based on Ibn Umar's statement.
Some later scholars may consider it absolutely prohibited due to humiliation.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? State the operative ruling.
The mufta bihi is permissible with dislike (makruh tanzihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز ان يشترى المسلم من الذمى ارض الخراج ويؤخذ منه الخراج
[۳۰۶۷) (۸۸) جائز ہے کہ مسلمان ذمی سے خراجی زمین خریدے اور اس سے خراج لیا جائے۔
عن ابن ابـي لـيـلـي قال اشترى الحسن بن على ملحة او ملحا واشترى الحسين بن على بريد ين من ارض الخراج وقال قد رد اليهم عمر ارضهم وصالحهم على الخراج (الف) ( سنن بیہقی ، باب من رخص في شراء ارض الخراج ، ج تاسع ،ص ۲۳۷، نمبر ۱۸۴۰۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ صحابہ نے خراجی زمین خریدی اور حضرت عمرؓ نے اس پر خراج لازم فرمایا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ابتدائی طور پر مسلمان پر خراج لازم کرنا صیح نہیں لیکن خراجی زمین خریدے گا تو اس کے واسطے سے مسلمان پر خراج لازم ہو جائے گا۔ نان حضرت عمر خراجی زمین خریدنے کو نا پسند فرماتے تھے۔ عن نافع ان عبد الله بن عمر كان اذا سئل عن الرجل من اهل الاسلام يأخذ الارض من اهل الذمة بما عليها من الخراج يقول لا يحل لمسلم او لا ينبغي لمسلم ان يكتب على نفسه الذل والصغار (ب) ( سنن بیہقی ، باب الارض اذا كانت صلحار قا بھالاصلها وعليها خراج و دونھا فا خذها منهم مسلم بكراء ، ج تاسع ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۸۳۹۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ خراجی زمین خرید نا ذلت کی چیز ہے۔
It is permissible for a Muslim to buy kharaj land from a dhimmi and kharaj is taken from him. (Section 88) It is permissible for a Muslim to buy kharaj land from a dhimmi and kharaj is taken from him. Ibn Abi Layla said: al-Hasan ibn Ali bought a salt mine or salt, and al-Husayn ibn Ali bought two barids of kharaj land, and he said: 'Umar returned their land to them and made peace with them on the kharaj.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: who permitted buying kharaj land, vol. 9, p. 237, no. 18405). From this athar it is known that the Companions bought kharaj land and Hadrat Umar imposed kharaj on it. Hence it is known that initially it is not correct to impose kharaj on a Muslim, but if he buys kharaj land, kharaj becomes binding on the Muslim through it. However, Hadrat Umar disliked buying kharaj land. From Nafi': Ibn Umar, when asked about a man from the People of Islam taking land from the People of Dhimma with the kharaj on it, said: 'It is not lawful for a Muslim, or it is not befitting for a Muslim, to write upon himself humiliation and lowliness.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, vol. 9, p. 236, no. 18397). This athar indicates that buying kharaj land is a thing of humiliation.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The ruling (88) permits a Muslim to buy kharaj land from a dhimmi, but the kharaj remains obligatory on the land. The author first states the ruling concisely in Arabic: 'It is permissible for a Muslim to buy kharaj land from a dhimmi and kharaj is taken from him.' Then the Urdu sharh expands: it is permissible, and kharaj is taken. The first proof (athar) reports that Hasan ibn Ali and Husayn ibn Ali bought kharaj land, and Umar imposed kharaj on them, showing that kharaj applies even to Muslims who purchase such land. The second athar from Ibn Umar indicates that buying kharaj land is disliked because it entails humiliation (dhull wa saghar), as kharaj is a form of subjugation. Thus the ruling is established: purchase is valid and kharaj must be paid, but it is makruh tanzihi due to the negative implication. This follows the principle that kharaj is a tax on land, not on the person, and buying the land transfers the obligation.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on non-Muslim-owned conquered lands; an obligation that remains on the land even if sold to a Muslim.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection with a covenant, paying jizya.
اثر (athar): A narration from a Sahabi (Companion), used as a proof (dalil).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a Muslim buying kharaj land from a dhimmi?
A) Absolutely prohibited because of humiliation
B) Permissible but disliked, and kharaj must be paid
C) Permissible without any dislike, and kharaj is waived
D) Prohibited because the land belongs to the state

Key Takeaway
A Muslim may buy kharaj land, but the kharaj remains due, and such purchase is disliked due to its association with humiliation.

Ruling on Contracts Made During Apostasy
Explains that contracts made during apostasy are suspended pending return to Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on transactions performed during apostasy and apply the rule to determine validity upon the apostate's return or death.

Core Idea
An apostate's contracts are suspended, not void; they become valid upon return to Islam.

This lesson explains the unique Hanafi position on transactions conducted by an apostate. Unlike other schools that deem them automatically void, the Hanafis suspend them pending the apostate's fate. Understanding this ruling clarifies the principle of suspended legal capacity (ahl al-mawquf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the transactions and their initial status
The text mentions sale, purchase, and any disposition of wealth during apostasy. Their legal status is 'mawquf' (suspended) — not immediately valid or void.
Suspension means validity depends on a future event.
2
Determine the outcome based on the apostate's subsequent status
If the apostate returns to Islam, the contracts become valid (sahih). If he dies, is killed, or flees to Dar al-Harb without returning, the contracts become void (batil).
Death includes being killed or joining enemy territory.
3
Understand the rationale
The apostate's ownership and legal capacity are suspended temporarily. If he returns, his capacity is restored retroactively; if not, he is considered dead from the moment of apostasy, so his contracts are invalid.
This is based on the principle that a dead person cannot transact.
4
Examine the supporting evidence
The text cites an athar from 'Amir and Al-Hakam concerning a married apostate. The marriage is suspended during iddah; if he returns before iddah ends, it remains valid. This indicates by analogy that other contracts are similarly suspended.
The athar is reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۱۰) و ما باعه او اشتراه او تصرف فيه من امواله في حال رَدّته موقوف فان اسلم صحت عقوده وان مات او قتل او لحق بدار الحرب بطلت تلك العقود۔

ارتداد کی حالت میں بیچا یا خریدا یا اپنے مال میں تصرف کیا تو یہ سب موقوف رہیں گے۔ پس اگر اسلام لے آیا تو یہ سب عقود صحیح
ہو جائیں گے۔ اور اگر مرتد کی حالت میں مرگیا یا قتل کر دیا گیا یا دار الحرب بھاگ گیا تو یہ تمام عقود باطل ہو جائیں گے۔ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ مرتد کی ملکیت اور اس کا معاملہ اسلام لانے تک موقف رہتا ہے۔ اگر اسلام لے آئے تو ملکیت اور معاملات بحال ہو جائیں گے۔ اور اسلام نہ لائے اور انتقال ہو جائے تو مرتد ہونے کے دن ہی سے مردہ شمار کیا جائے گا۔ جس کی وجہ سے ارتداد کے بعد کے معاملات باطل ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ مردوں کے معاملات کا کیا اعتبار ؟

(۲) اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عامر والحكم قالا في الرجل المسلم يرتد عن الاسلام ويلحق بارض العدو فلتعتد امرأته ثلاثة قروء ان كانت تحيض، وان كانت لا تحيض فثلاثة اشهر، وان كانت حاملا ان تضع حملها ويقسم ميراثه بين امرأته وورثته من المسلمين ثم تزوج ان شاءت وان هو رجع فتاب من قبل ان تنقضي عدتها ثبتا على نكاحهما (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ، ۳۱ ما قالوافی المرتد اذ الحق بارض العدو وله امرأة ما حالهما ، ج سادس، ص ۴۴۵، نمبر ۳۲۷۵۲) اس اثر کے اخیر میں ہے کہ اگر مرتد بیوی کی عدت ختم ہونے سے پہلے تو بہ کرنے اور اسلام لے آئے تو دونوں کا نکاح بحال رہے گا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عدت ختم ہونے تک نکاح کا معاملہ موقوف رہے گا۔ اور اسی پر قیاس
(110) And whatever he sold or bought or disposed of from his wealth in the state of apostasy is suspended. If he becomes Muslim, his contracts become valid; and if he dies, or is killed, or joins Dar al-Harb, those contracts become void. During apostasy, if he sells, buys, or disposes of his wealth, all of this remains suspended. Then if he becomes Muslim, all these contracts become valid. And if during apostasy he dies, or is killed, or flees to Dar al-Harb, then all these contracts become void. It has already passed that the ownership of the apostate and his affairs remain suspended until he becomes Muslim. If he becomes Muslim, his ownership and transactions are restored. And if he does not become Muslim and passes away, then from the day of his apostasy he is counted as dead. Because of this, transactions after apostasy are void. For what reliance is there on the transactions of the dead? There is an indication of this in the athar: From 'Amir and Al-Hakam concerning a Muslim man who apostatizes from Islam and joins enemy territory... (the same athar as before). At the end of this athar it mentions that if the apostate returns and repents before the wife's 'iddah expires, their marriage remains. This shows that the marriage remains suspended until the 'iddah ends. And analogy is made upon this.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This is a ruling statement passage. The author presents the second legal rule concerning an apostate who joins Dar al-Harb: all his transactions during apostasy (sales, purchases, other dispositions) are suspended (mawquf). If he later returns to Islam, these contracts become valid retroactively. If he dies, is killed, or flees to Dar al-Harb, the contracts are void. The commentary explains the rationale: the apostate's ownership and legal capacity are suspended pending his return to Islam. If he returns, his capacity is restored and transactions are validated. If he does not, he is legally dead from the moment of apostasy, so his transactions are invalid because a dead person's contracts have no legal effect. The proof is the same athar from 'Amir and Al-Hakam, which shows that the marriage (a contract) is suspended during the 'iddah period: if he returns before the 'iddah ends, the marriage remains valid; otherwise it is dissolved. This indicates by analogy that other contracts are similarly suspended.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; the contract's validity is contingent on the apostate's return to Islam.
عقود (uqud): Contracts, including sales, purchases, and other legal transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a sale made by an apostate during his apostasy if he later returns to Islam?
A) The sale is void because apostasy invalidates all transactions.
B) The sale becomes valid because his ownership is restored.
C) The sale remains suspended forever.
D) The sale is valid only if the buyer was Muslim.

Key Takeaway
An apostate's contracts are suspended pending return to Islam; they become valid upon return and void upon death or permanent departure.

Spending of Public Funds: Kharaj, Jizya, and Other Revenues
Ruling on spending collected funds for Muslim welfare

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that kharaj, jizya, and similar public funds must be spent for general Muslim welfare, and list the specific categories of expenditure.

Core Idea
Kharaj and jizya are public welfare funds, not ritual alms – they finance borders, judges, scholars, and warriors.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi ruling on the allocation of state revenues collected from land tax (kharaj), poll tax (jizya), special tribute from Banu Taghlib, and gifts from hostile rulers. Unlike zakat, which has fixed recipients, these funds are classified as general public treasury and must be spent on the collective needs of the Muslim community. The passage lists specific permissible expenditures, such as fortifying borders and paying salaries to judges and scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the revenue sources
Locate the four types of funds mentioned: kharaj, Banu Taghlib wealth, gifts from harbis, and jizya. Understand that these are distinct from zakat and 'ushr.
Kharaj is a land tax, jizya is a head tax on dhimmis.
2
State the general ruling
The imam must spend these funds for the welfare (masalih) of the Muslims. This is wajib (obligatory) because it is a communal duty.
Welfare here includes defensive, infrastructural, and administrative needs.
3
List the specific expenditures
The passage mentions: fortifying borders (thughur), building bridges and arches (qanatir, jusur), paying salaries to judges, officials, and scholars, and providing allowances for warriors (muqatila) and their dependents.
These categories are not exhaustive but illustrative.
4
Understand the legal nature
These funds are not 'ibadat (acts of worship) like zakat, so they are not restricted to specific recipients. They are secular public funds for the common good.
The term 'nawa'ib al-muslimin' encompasses all public needs and calamities.
5
Locate the proof
The hadith from Abu Dawood shows the Prophet (PBUH) setting aside half of the booty for public needs. By qiyas, kharaj and jizya are also used for such purposes.
The hadith strengthens the analogy that public funds serve general welfare.

پل مقاتلة : قال سے مشتق ہے جہاد کرنے والے، ذراری : ذریۃ سے مشتق ہے اولاد ۔ حاشیه : (الف) غنیمت کا باقی آدھا الگ رکھا آنے والے وفود کے لئے اور معاملات کے لئے اور لوگوں کے مصائب میں مدد کے لئے۔
What the imam collects from kharaj, from the wealth of Banu Taghlib, and what the people of war gift to the imam, and jizya, are spent for the welfare of the Muslims. From it, the border posts are fortified, bridges and arches are built. From it, the judges of the Muslims, their officials, and their scholars are given enough to suffice them, and from it is paid. In this effect it is that Hadrat Umar made peace at double the zakat, and zakat is one dirham in forty dirhams, so its double becomes one dirham in twenty dirhams. And zakat is due on both men and women, so this kharaj is also due on both men and women. And zakat is not on children, so this kharaj is also not on children. Imam Shafi'i says: Banu Taghlib are dhimmis, and kharaj is due on dhimmis even if zakat is imposed. And jizya is not on women and children, so this also will not be on women and children. Banu Taghlib is the name of a tribe with whom Hadrat Umar made peace at double zakat; now this tribe does not exist. What the imam collected from kharaj, from the wealth of Banu Taghlib, and what the people of war gave as a gift and jizya, he will spend for the welfare of the Muslims. So from it border posts will be fortified, bridges will be built. From it, the judges of the Muslims, their officials, and their scholars will be given as much as suffices them. And from it will be paid the daily allowance of warriors and their children. The wealth of kharaj, the wealth of Banu Taghlib, the gift of the people of war, and jizya are not like 'ushr as wealth of worship, so these wealths should be spent for the benefit of the Muslims. For example, the borders with disbelievers should be fortified, bridges built, the judges of the Muslims given daily sustenance and salary so that they and their children are sufficed. Similarly, those who work for the Muslims, or the scholars who do the work of conveying the religion, or the mujahideen engaged in jihad, should be given enough daily sustenance for them and their children. Because these people are working for the benefit of the Muslims. And all the above wealths are spent in these works. All these works are called Nawa'ib al-Muslimin. (2) There is proof of this in hadith: from Bashir ibn Yasar, the mawla of the Ansar, ... and he set aside the remaining half for delegations that came to him, for affairs, and for the calamities of people. (Abu Dawood, Bab ma ja'a fi hukm ard Khaybar, p.68 no.3012). From this hadith it is known that the wealth of ghanimah can also be kept for Nawa'ib al-Muslimin. So by analogy, the wealth of kharaj etc. will also be spent in the affairs of Muslims. Jabah: received, collected. Sadd: derived from 'sadd' meaning to block. Thughur: plural of thaghr, border. Qanatir: plural of qantara, bridge. Jisr: bridge. Muqatila: derived from qitl, one who does jihad. Dhurari: derived from dhurriyyah, children. Annotation (a): The remaining half of ghanimah was set aside for the delegations that came, for affairs, and for helping people in calamities.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on how the imam should spend funds collected from kharaj, Banu Taghlib's wealth, gifts from harbi enemies, and jizya. The ruling states that these funds are not like zakat or 'ushr (which are acts of worship with specific recipients), but rather are general public funds for the welfare of Muslims. The imam must spend them on fortifying borders, building bridges, and providing salaries for judges, officials, scholars, and warriors with their dependents. The commentary then discusses a subsidiary issue: the status of Banu Taghlib, a Christian Arab tribe with whom Hadrat Umar made peace at double zakat instead of jizya. The Hanafi position, following Umar's precedent, treats this as a fixed tribute that applies to men and women (like zakat) but not to children. Imam Shafi'i argues that Banu Taghlib are dhimmis and thus subject to kharaj (which applies to land) but not to jizya on women and children; however, the Hanafis maintain that the treaty is specific. The commentary then emphasizes that all such funds are secular public welfare, not ritual. It cites a hadith from Abu Dawood where the Prophet (PBUH) set aside half of the war booty for public needs (Nawa'ib al-Muslimin), and applies qiyas to kharaj funds. The note explains key terms like thughur (borders) and qanatir (bridges).

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on conquered lands, distinct from jizya and zakat.
جزیہ (jizya): Poll tax on dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) in exchange for protection.
نوائب المسلمین (nawa'ib al-muslimin): Public needs and calamities of the Muslim community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, which of the following is a wajib use of kharaj funds?
A) Giving exclusively to the poor and needy (fuqara and masakin)
B) Building bridges and fortifying borders
C) Distributing equally among all Muslims
D) Spending only on scholars

Key Takeaway
Kharaj and jizya are secular public welfare funds, not ritual alms; they must be spent on the collective needs of the Muslim community.

The Case of Banu Taghlib: Double Zakat vs Jizya
Dispute on taxation of Banu Taghlib between Hanafi and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the taxation of Banu Taghlib as double zakat, contrast it with the Shafi'i view, and identify the practical difference (thamarah) between the two positions.

Core Idea
Banu Taghlib pay double zakat (not jizya) by Umar's treaty – a distinct category of tribute applied to men and women, not children.

The passage includes a subsidiary discussion on the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib, with whom Caliph Umar (RA) made a peace treaty at double the zakat rate. This lesson focuses on the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the legal nature of this tribute. The Hanafis treat it as a fixed levy analogous to zakat, while Shafi'is argue it should follow jizya rules. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the schools derive rulings from historical precedents.

Guided Path
1
Recall who Banu Taghlib were
Banu Taghlib was a Christian Arab tribe. Caliph Umar made peace with them at double the zakat rate (1/20 of wealth) instead of jizya or kharaj.
This historical treaty is the basis of the Hanafi ruling.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The double zakat applies to both men and women (like zakat) but not to children (like zakat). It is not considered jizya but a fixed tribute.
Qiyas on zakat: zakat is on men and women, not on children.
3
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam Shafi'i argues that Banu Taghlib are dhimmis, so they should pay kharaj (land tax) and jizya (on free adult males only). Therefore, the tribute should not apply to women and children.
Shafi'i view: the treaty of Umar is not a general rule.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the treaty is specific and does not imply a general rule. Since the tribe no longer exists, the ruling remains as a historical precedent but not a model for other dhimmis.
The disagreement is legitimate (ikhtilaf) and both positions have strong evidence.
5
Determine the practical difference
Under Hanafi law, Banu Taghlib (if existed) would pay double zakat on all adults; under Shafi'i law, only adult males would pay jizya, and land would be subject to kharaj.
The thamarah is the rate and base of taxation.

عاملوں کو اور ان کے علماء کو جتنا ان کو کافی ہو۔ اور دیا جائے گا اس سے غازیوں اور ان کی اولا د کا روزینہ۔ ۔  خراج کا مال، بنی تغلب کا مال ، حربیوں کا ہدیہ اور جزیہ وغیرہ عشر کی طرح عبادت والا مال نہیں جائے۔ اسی طرح جو لوگ مسلمانوں کے لئے کام کرتے ہوں یا وہ علماء جو تبلیغ دین کا کام کرتے ہوں یا جو مجاہدین جہاد میں مشغول ہیں ان کے لئے اور ان کی اولاد کے لئے جتنی روزی کافی ہو وہ ادا کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ لوگ مسلمانوں کے فائدے کے لئے کام کر رہے ہیں۔ اور اوپر کے سب مال انہیں کاموں میں خرچ کئے جاتے ہیں۔ ان سب کاموں کو نوائب المسلمین کہتے ہیں (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن بشير بن يسار مولى الانصار ... وعزل النصف الباقي لمن نزل به من الوفود والامور ونوائب الناس (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فی حکم ارض خیبر، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۰۱۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال غنیمت بھی نوائب المسلمین کے لئے رکھا جا سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے خراج کا مال وغیرہ بھی امور سور مسلمین میں خرچ کیا جائے گا۔ جباه : وصول کیا، جمع کیا، تد : سد سے مشتق ہے بند کرنا، الشغور : ثغر کی جمع ہے سرحد، القناطر : قطرة کی جمع ہے پل، جسر پل مقاتلة : قال سے مشتق ہے جہاد کرنے والے، ذراری : ذریۃ سے مشتق ہے اولاد ۔ حاشیه : (الف) غنیمت کا باقی آدھا الگ رکھا آنے والے وفود کے لئے اور معاملات کے لئے اور لوگوں کے مصائب میں مدد کے لئے۔
What the imam collects from kharaj, from the wealth of Banu Taghlib, and what the people of war gift to the imam, and jizya, are spent for the welfare of the Muslims. From it, the border posts are fortified, bridges and arches are built. From it, the judges of the Muslims, their officials, and their scholars are given enough to suffice them, and from it is paid. In this effect it is that Hadrat Umar made peace at double the zakat, and zakat is one dirham in forty dirhams, so its double becomes one dirham in twenty dirhams. And zakat is due on both men and women, so this kharaj is also due on both men and women. And zakat is not on children, so this kharaj is also not on children. Imam Shafi'i says: Banu Taghlib are dhimmis, and kharaj is due on dhimmis even if zakat is imposed. And jizya is not on women and children, so this also will not be on women and children. Banu Taghlib is the name of a tribe with whom Hadrat Umar made peace at double zakat; now this tribe does not exist. What the imam collected from kharaj, from the wealth of Banu Taghlib, and what the people of war gave as a gift and jizya, he will spend for the welfare of the Muslims. So from it border posts will be fortified, bridges will be built. From it, the judges of the Muslims, their officials, and their scholars will be given as much as suffices them. And from it will be paid the daily allowance of warriors and their children. The wealth of kharaj, the wealth of Banu Taghlib, the gift of the people of war, and jizya are not like 'ushr as wealth of worship, so these wealths should be spent for the benefit of the Muslims. For example, the borders with disbelievers should be fortified, bridges built, the judges of the Muslims given daily sustenance and salary so that they and their children are sufficed. Similarly, those who work for the Muslims, or the scholars who do the work of conveying the religion, or the mujahideen engaged in jihad, should be given enough daily sustenance for them and their children. Because these people are working for the benefit of the Muslims. And all the above wealths are spent in these works. All these works are called Nawa'ib al-Muslimin. (2) There is proof of this in hadith: from Bashir ibn Yasar, the mawla of the Ansar, ... and he set aside the remaining half for delegations that came to him, for affairs, and for the calamities of people. (Abu Dawood, Bab ma ja'a fi hukm ard Khaybar, p.68 no.3012). From this hadith it is known that the wealth of ghanimah can also be kept for Nawa'ib al-Muslimin. So by analogy, the wealth of kharaj etc. will also be spent in the affairs of Muslims. Jabah: received, collected. Sadd: derived from 'sadd' meaning to block. Thughur: plural of thaghr, border. Qanatir: plural of qantara, bridge. Jisr: bridge. Muqatila: derived from qitl, one who does jihad. Dhurari: derived from dhurriyyah, children. Annotation (a): The remaining half of ghanimah was set aside for the delegations that came, for affairs, and for helping people in calamities.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on how the imam should spend funds collected from kharaj, Banu Taghlib's wealth, gifts from harbi enemies, and jizya. The ruling states that these funds are not like zakat or 'ushr (which are acts of worship with specific recipients), but rather are general public funds for the welfare of Muslims. The imam must spend them on fortifying borders, building bridges, and providing salaries for judges, officials, scholars, and warriors with their dependents. The commentary then discusses a subsidiary issue: the status of Banu Taghlib, a Christian Arab tribe with whom Hadrat Umar made peace at double zakat instead of jizya. The Hanafi position, following Umar's precedent, treats this as a fixed tribute that applies to men and women (like zakat) but not to children. Imam Shafi'i argues that Banu Taghlib are dhimmis and thus subject to kharaj (which applies to land) but not to jizya on women and children; however, the Hanafis maintain that the treaty is specific. The commentary then emphasizes that all such funds are secular public welfare, not ritual. It cites a hadith from Abu Dawood where the Prophet (PBUH) set aside half of the war booty for public needs (Nawa'ib al-Muslimin), and applies qiyas to kharaj funds. The note explains key terms like thughur (borders) and qanatir (bridges).

Key Terms
بني تغلب (Banu Taghlib): A Christian Arab tribe with whom Caliph Umar made a peace treaty at double zakat.
صلح (sulh): Peace treaty or settlement, often used for arrangements with non-Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who from Banu Taghlib is liable to pay the double zakat?
A) Only adult men
B) Adult men and women, but not children
C) All members including children
D) Only the chief of the tribe

Key Takeaway
Banu Taghlib's double zakat is a historical Hanafi ruling based on Umar's precedent, distinct from jizya and applicable only to that tribe.

Using Silver-Plated Utensils and Furniture: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on permissibility of silver-plated items per Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on silver-plated items and identify the key evidence used.

Core Idea
Silver-plated items are permissible; only pure silver utensils are prohibited.

This passage from the Book of Prohibition and Permission addresses a common question: may Muslims use vessels or furniture that have silver inlaid or attached? While general hadith warn against using gold and silver vessels, Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between pure silver items and those merely decorated or repaired with silver. By examining prophetic practice, we see that small amounts of silver for repair or decoration are permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Drinking from a silver-plated vessel, riding a silver-plated saddle, sitting on a silver-plated bed. According to Abu Hanifa, these are permissible (mubah).
The ruling is not for items made entirely of silver.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: the Prophet's cup that cracked and was mended with silver, and his sword hilt that had silver. These are found in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
Both hadith are ahad (single-narrator), thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actions demonstrate permissibility. If using a silver-mended cup or a silver-hilted sword were prohibited, he would not have done so. Therefore, silver for repair or decoration is allowed.
Abu Hanifa uses these as evidence that the general prohibition on silver vessels applies only to items made entirely of silver.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf holds it makruh due to general prohibitions (e.g., 'Do not drink from gold and silver vessels'). Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold it haram absolutely.
The difference hinges on whether the general hadith are applied to all silver or just pure silver.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author presents Abu Hanifa's view first and supports it with hadith, indicating it is the mufta bihi (operative position). The permissive view is relied upon in the Hanafi school.
The practical consequence: Hanafis may use silver-plated items, while other schools may not.

Source Text

كتاب الحظر والاباحة
[ ٣١١١] (١١) ويجوز الشرب فى الاناء المفضّض عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى والركوب على السرج المفضض والجلوس على السرير المفضض ٣١١٢) (۱۲) و [۳۱۱۱] (۱۱) جائز ہے چاندی چڑھے برتن میں پینا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور جائز ہے چاندی چڑھے زین پر سوار ہونا ، اور چاندی چڑھے تخت پر بیٹھنا۔ چیز چاندی کی نہ ہولیکن کہیں کہیں چاندی لگی ہوئی ہو تو اس کا استعمال کرنا جائز ہے۔ مثلا برتن میں کہیں کہیں چاندی لگی ہوئی ہے یا تخت پر کہیں کہیں چاندی لگی ہوئی ہے یا گھوڑے کی زمین پر چاندی لگی ہوئی ہے تو ان کا استعمال کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور اتنی ہی چاندی درست ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور کا ٹوٹا ہوا پیالہ چاندی سے باندھا ہوا تھا۔ حضور کی تلوار کے دستے پر چاندی تھی۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عاصم الاحـول قـال رأيـت قـدح النبي الله عند انس بن مالك و كان قد انصدع فسلسله بفضة ،قال وهو قدح جيد عريض من نضار ، قال قال انس لقد سقيت رسول الله الله الله في هذا القدح اكثر من " كذا وكذا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشرب من قدح النبي له وانیت ، ص ۸۴۲ نمبر ۵۶۳۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ برتن کو چاندی سے باندھا ہو تو اس کو استعمال کرنا جائز ہے۔ ابوداؤد شریف میں ہے۔ عن انس قال كانت قبيعة سيف رسول الله له فضة (ب) ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی السیف محلی ص ۷۲۸، نمبر ۲۵۸۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور کی تلوار کے دستے میں چاندی تھی ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ زمین وغیرہ پر تھوڑی چاندی ہو تو جائز ہے۔ اننده امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک چاندی کی ممانعت کی عام احادیث کی وجہ سے مکروہ ہے۔ المفضض : فضہ سے مشتق ہے چاندی جڑی ہوئی، سرج : زین، سریر : تخت۔
Book of Prohibition and Permission. [3111] (11) It is permissible to drink from a silver-plated vessel according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), and to ride on a silver-plated saddle, and to sit on a silver-plated bed. And [3111] (11) It is permissible to drink from a silver-plated vessel according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and it is permissible to ride on a silver-plated saddle, and to sit on a silver-plated bed. The object is not made of silver, but wherever silver is attached, its use is permissible. For example, a vessel has silver attached in some places, or a bed has silver attached in some places, or a horse's saddle has silver attached, then using them is permissible. And that much silver is fine. In hadith: The Prophet's broken bowl was bound with silver. The Prophet's sword hilt had silver. The hadith is: 'Asim al-Ahwal said: I saw the Prophet's cup with Anas ibn Malik, and it had cracked so he mended it with silver. He said: It was a good wide cup of nard wood. Anas said: I gave the Messenger of Allah to drink from this cup more than such and such (times) (Bukhari, chapter on drinking from the Prophet's cup and vessel, p.842 no.5638). From this hadith it is understood that if a vessel is bound with silver, using it is permissible. In Abu Dawud: Anas said: The hilt of the Messenger of Allah's sword was silver (Abu Dawud, chapter on the sword with silver, p.728 no.2583). From this hadith it is understood that the Prophet's sword hilt had silver. From this it is understood that if there is a little silver on the saddle etc., it is permissible. However, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, due to the general hadith prohibiting silver, it is makruh. al-mufaddad: derived from fidda, meaning silver-inlaid, sarj: saddle, sarir: bed.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Book of Prohibition and Permission. It states the position of Imam Abu Hanifa on the use of silver-plated (not pure silver) items: drinking vessels, saddles, and beds. The author clarifies that the item itself is not made of silver but has silver attached in places; such use is permissible. He then provides evidence from hadith: the Prophet's mended cup (bound with silver) and his sword hilt (silver). These show that small amounts of silver for repair or decoration are allowed. However, the commentary notes that Imam Abu Yusuf considers this makruh (disliked) due to general prohibitions on using silver vessels. The passage ends with definitions: mufaddad = silver-inlaid, sarj = saddle, sarir = bed.

Key Terms
المفضّض (al-mufaddad): An object that has silver inlaid or attached, not made entirely of silver.
السرج (al-sarj): Saddle for riding a horse or other animal.
السرير (al-sarir): Bed or throne; a piece of furniture for sitting or lying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on drinking from a silver-plated vessel?
A) Haram because it contains silver.
B) Makruh tanzihi.
C) Mubah (permissible) because the silver is only attached for repair or decoration.
D) Mustahab because the Prophet used such a vessel.

Key Takeaway
Silver-plated items are permissible because the silver is for repair/decoration, as shown by the Prophet's practice.

Looking at and Touching Another's Slave Woman
Ruling with proof on permissible looking and touching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at and touching another man's slave woman and explain the distinction between general prohibition and the purchase exception.

Core Idea
Touching a slave woman is forbidden due to desire, except when examining for purchase.

The Hanafi school balances practical needs with the prohibition of unlawful touch. While looking at another man's slave woman is permitted to the same extent as a mahram, touching those same parts is generally forbidden because desire is fully present. However, the law makes an exception for a potential buyer: he may touch her to assess her physical condition, even if desire arises, because she is considered property and examination is a necessity. In this lesson, we will analyse the ruling, its evidence, and the precise condition that changes the hukm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on two acts: looking at and touching another man's slave woman. Looking is mubah for head, arms, shins (same as mahram). Touching is generally haram because desire is fully present, but becomes mubah if the man intends to purchase her.
The term 'shahwat kamilah' is key: it refers to the presence of desire without the deterrence of respect that exists with mahram relatives.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two types of evidence: (1) Hadith and athar showing that a slave woman's head is not 'awrah, establishing the permissible scope for looking. (2) The hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'There is no harm for a man to turn over a slave girl if he wants to buy her and look at her except her private parts.' This implicitly permits touching for examination.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi; its chain is considered strong.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the hadith of Ibn Abbas, the phrase 'yqallib' (turn over) implies handling and touching. Since the hadith permits turning over for examination, touching is implicitly allowed during that process. The restriction 'except her private parts' defines the limit of looking and by extension touching.
The Hanafi view that a slave woman's 'awrah for looking is from navel to knee is supported by the athar about her praying without a head covering.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position that a slave woman's 'awrah is limited (navel to knee, head not 'awrah) is mukhtalaf fih. Other schools may consider her entire body 'awrah, thus prohibiting both looking and touching entirely.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): other schools would not permit even the looking that Hanafis allow, and certainly not touching for purchase.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school. It is based on the necessity of slave women working outside the home and the need for buyers to examine property. The hadith evidence supports this practical ruling.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani all agree on this ruling.

Source Text

اشارہ ہے۔ حسن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا بأس ان يقلب الرجل الجارية اذا اراد ان يشتريها و ينظر اليها ماخلا عورتها (د) (سن للبیہقی ، باب عورة الامتہ ض ثانی ص ۳۲۱، نمبر ۳۲۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ باندی کو خریدنے کا ارادہ ہو تو اس کو الٹ پلٹ کر دیکھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اور الٹنے پلٹتے وقت چھونا بھی ہوگا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ چھوسکتا ہے۔ حاشیه : (الف) حضور نے فرمایا اللہ نے ابن آدم پر زنا کا حصہ لکھ دیا ہے جو ہونے ہی والا ہے۔ پس دونوں آنکھوں کا زنا دیکھتا ہے، اور دونوں کانوں کا زنا سننا ہے، اور زبان کا زنا بات کرنا ہے، اور ہاتھ کا زنا چھوٹا ہے، اور پاؤں کا زنا چلتا ہے، اور دل خواہش کرتا ہے اور تمنا کرتا ہے اور فرج اس کی تصدیق کرتا ہے یا تکذیب کرتا ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا باندی سر کی اوڑھنی ڈال سکتی ہے (ج) حضرت ابراهیم نے فرمایا ام ولد بغیر اور معنی کے نماز پڑھ سکتی ہے چاہے ساٹھ سال کی ہو چکی ہو ( د) حضور نے فرمایا باندی کو الٹ پلٹ کر دیکھے اس میں حرج نہیں ہے اگر اس کو خریدنا چاہتا ہو، اور ستر کے علاوہ دیکھ سکتا ہے۔
He may look at her from it, and a man may look at another's slave woman to the extent that he may look at his mahram women [3128] (28) And there is no harm in touching that if he intends to buy, even if he fears desire. [3127] (27) A man may see from another's slave woman as much of her body as he may see from his own mahram women. From a mahram woman, looking from the collarbone to the knee is not permissible; the rest—head, arms, and shins—he may see. Similarly, from another's slave woman, looking from the collarbone to the knee is not permissible; the rest—head, arms, and shins—he may see. A slave woman will go out to work, so it would be difficult for her to keep a head covering at all times. Therefore there is leeway for her to keep her head, arms, and shins uncovered. (2) She is like a mahram woman in that regard. However, touching those parts that are permissible to look at is not permissible, because there is complete desire there. (3) There is proof in a hadith: `Ata' said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, the slave woman may let down the covering of her head.' (b) And in another athar: Ibrahim said: 'The umm al-walad may pray without a head covering even if she has reached sixty years of age.' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no.62266? 6234? vol.2 p.141). From this hadith and athar it is understood that the head of a slave woman, and by analogy the arms and shins, is not 'awrah. [3128] (28) There is no harm in touching these parts if he intends to buy, even if he fears desire. If one intends to buy a slave woman, then even if there is fear of desire arising from touching, he may still touch those parts that he is allowed to look at. For example, he may see her head, arms, or shins, and if he intends to buy, he may also touch them to ascertain her softness and texture. A slave woman is in the category of property, so out of necessity he may touch her to examine. (2) There is an indication of this in a hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no harm for a man to turn over a slave girl if he wants to buy her and look at her except her private parts.' (d) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab `awrat al-ammah, vol.2 p.321 no.3224). This hadith states that when intending to buy a slave girl, there is no harm in turning her over to look, and by necessity that involves touching, so it is permissible. Margin notes: (a) The Prophet said: Allah has decreed for the son of Adam his share of zina which he inevitably encounters. The zina of the eyes is looking, of the ears is listening, of the tongue is speaking, of the hand is striking, of the foot is walking. The heart desires and wishes, and the private parts confirm or deny that. (b )The Prophet said: The slave woman may let down the covering of her head. (c) Ibrahim said: The umm al-walad may pray without a head covering even if she is sixty years old. (d) The Prophet said: There is no harm in turning a slave girl to look at her if he intends to buy her, and he may look at her except her private parts.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh al-Sameri addresses the rules regarding looking at and touching a slave woman belonging to another person. It begins by establishing that a man may look at another's slave woman to the same extent as his own mahram women: he may see her head, arms, and shins, but not from the collarbone to the knee. The reason given is practical: slave women work outside the home, so strict covering of the head would cause hardship. Therefore, like mahram women, slave women are permitted to keep those parts uncovered. However, there is an important distinction: while looking is permissible as with mahram, touching those body parts is generally not permissible because desire is fully present (unlike mahram where respect deters desire). The exception is when one intends to purchase the slave woman: then touching is allowed to assess her physical condition, even if desire arises, because she is property and necessity demands examination. Evidence is provided from a hadith of Imam Ata' and an athar from Ibrahim regarding the head covering of a slave woman in prayer, establishing that her head is not 'awrah. Also, the hadith of Ibn Abbas about turning a slave girl when buying confirms that touching is implicitly permitted for examination.

Key Terms
باندی (bandi): A slave woman owned by another person; subject to different rules of 'awrah and touching than free women.
شہوت کاملہ (shahwat kamilah): Complete desire; the state where desire is fully present without the deterrence of respect (as with mahram).
اراد شراء (iradat al-shira): Intention to purchase; a condition that permits touching a slave woman even if desire arises, due to necessity of examination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this lesson, when is it permissible for a man to touch the head of another man's slave woman?
A) At any time, as long as he does not feel desire.
B) Only when he intends to purchase her.
C) Only if she gives permission.
D) Never, because a slave woman's head is 'awrah.

Key Takeaway
A man may look at another's slave woman as he looks at his mahram, but may only touch her if he intends to purchase her.

Touching a Female Slave for Purchase: Permissibility Despite Desire
Ruling on touching a female slave's permissible parts when intending to purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching a female slave when intending to buy and evaluate the conflicting narration regarding desire.

Core Idea
Touching a female slave for purchase is permissible despite potential desire; need overrides general prohibition of lustful touch.

When purchasing a human being (slave), physical inspection is necessary. Islamic law balances this need with the prohibition of unlawful touch. In this passage, the author presents the primary ruling that touching permissible parts is allowed when intending to buy, even if desire may arise, but then introduces a conflicting narration that prohibits touching if desire is feared. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to weigh competing proofs in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the primary ruling
Identify the act (touching a female slave's permissible parts) and the ruling: mubah (permissible) when intending to buy.
The phrase 'ولا بأس' indicates no harm, i.e., permissibility.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith: 'لا بأس ان يقلب الرجل الجارية اذا اراد ان يشتريها' – explicit permission to turn over and look, which includes touching.
This is a hadith from Bayhaqi, classed as zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala.
3
Understand the second narration
Another narration states: if desire is feared, touching the slave is not permissible. This creates an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The basis is the hadith equating lustful touch with zina of the hand.
4
Analyze the conflict
The author presents both but implies the first is the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah). The need for purchase justifies the touch, overriding the general prohibition of lustful contact.
The second narration may be a weaker transmission or a precautionary view.
5
Derive the mufta bihi
The primary position (permissible despite desire) is mufta bihi, as it is supported by explicit hadith and the principle of need (ḥāja).
This is the position adopted in later Hanafi fatwa works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۲۸] (۲۸) ولا بأس بان يمس ذلك اذا اراد الشراء وان والقلب يهوى ويتمنى ويصدق ذلك الفرج ويكذبه (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب قدر علی ابن آدم حظه من الزنا وغیرہ ،ص۳۳۶، نمبر ۷ ۶۷۵۴/۲۶۵/ بخاری شریف، باب زنا الجوارح دون الفرج ، ص ۹۲۲، نمبر ۶۲۴۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ شہوت کے ساتھ پکڑنا بھی زنا کے درجے میں ہے اس لئے شہوت ہو تو ذی رحم محرم کے ان اعضاء کو نہ چھوئے۔ ت مس : چھونا۔ اور دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ شہوت کا اندیشہ ہو تو باندی کو چھونا جائز نہیں۔ پہلے گزر چکا کہ شہوت کے ساتھ چھونا ہاتھ کا زنا ہے والید زناها البطش (مسلم شریف، نمبر ۲۶۵۷) اس لئے دوسرے کے مال سے زنا کے انداز کا استفادہ جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
حاشیه : (الف) حضور نے فرمایا اللہ نے ابن آدم پر زنا کا حصہ لکھ دیا ہے جو ہونے ہی والا ہے۔ پس دونوں آنکھوں کا زنا دیکھتا ہے، اور دونوں کانوں کا زنا سننا ہے، اور زبان کا زنا بات کرنا ہے، اور ہاتھ کا زنا چھوٹا ہے، اور پاؤں کا زنا چلتا ہے، اور دل خواہش کرتا ہے اور تمنا کرتا ہے اور فرج اس کی تصدیق کرتا ہے یا تکذیب کرتا ہے
(د) حضور نے فرمایا باندی کو الٹ پلٹ کر دیکھے اس میں حرج نہیں ہے اگر اس کو خریدنا چاہتا ہو، اور ستر کے علاوہ دیکھ سکتا ہے۔
There is no harm in touching that when he intends to buy, even if the heart desires and wishes and the private part confirms or denies it. (alif) (Muslim, etc.) This hadith indicates that touching with desire is also a type of zina, so if there is desire, do not touch those parts of mahram women. (tams: touching). And in another narration, if desire is feared, touching the female slave is not permissible. It has passed earlier that touching with desire is zina of the hand, 'the zina of the hand is the touch,' so benefiting from another's property in a manner of zina is not permissible.
Footnote (alif): The Prophet said, 'Allah has decreed for the son of Adam his share of zina which inevitably occurs. The zina of the eyes is looking, the zina of the ears is listening, the zina of the tongue is speaking, the zina of the hand is touching, the zina of the foot is walking, and the heart desires and wishes, and the private part confirms or denies it.'
Footnote (dal): The Prophet said, 'There is no harm for a man to turn over a slave-girl when he intends to buy her and look at her except her private parts.'
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical scenario: a man intends to buy a female slave and needs to assess her physically. The primary ruling is that there is no harm in touching her permissible parts (head, arms, shins) even if desire might arise, because the purchase need justifies it. The author then cites a hadith that equates touching with desire to zina, warning against touching mahram women with desire. For the female slave, however, the need for purchase permits it. But a second narration is presented that prohibits touching if desire is feared, based on the principle that touching with desire is zina of the hand. The author resolves by indicating the necessity: since the female slave is property, the need for purchase overrides the general prohibition. Footnotes provide the full hadiths: one enumerating the zina of the limbs, and another specifically allowing turning over and looking at a slave-girl for purchase except her private parts.

Key Terms
شہوت کاملہ (shahwat kamilah): Complete or strong desire, presumably leading to arousal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary ruling on touching a female slave's permissible parts when one intends to buy her?
A) It is absolutely prohibited
B) It is permissible without any condition
C) It is permissible even if desire is feared
D) It is only permissible if there is no desire

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits touching a female slave's permissible parts when intending to purchase, despite potential desire, as the need for assessment takes precedence over the general prohibition of lustful touch.

The Ruling on Hoarding (Ihtikar) in the Hanafi School
Ruling on hoarding food for humans and animals causing harm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hoarding essential foodstuffs, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding non-essential items, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Hoarding essential foodstuffs is makruh tahrimi; the dispute is whether non-essentials also count when need is dire.

This lesson examines the ruling on ihtikar (hoarding) in Hanafi fiqh. While it is generally disliked to hoard essential foodstuffs that cause hardship, a disagreement exists between Imam Abu Hanifa and his student Imam Abu Yusuf concerning items beyond basic food. We will explore the evidence and the practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
The text states that hoarding food for humans and animals in a town where it causes harm is makruh. Understand the conditions: the items must be essential foodstuffs (aqwat), and the hoarding must cause harm to the people.
2
Locate the Dispute
After stating the ruling, the text raises the question: what about items other than human food and animal feed? Is hoarding those also makruh? This is the point of disagreement.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that hoarding non-essential items is not makruh. His evidence is that the hadith and athar specifically mention 'aqwat' (foodstuffs), so the ruling is limited to that.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
4
Understand Abu Yusuf's Position
Imam Abu Yusuf says that if the townspeople are in dire need of a particular item, then hoarding it is also makruh. His basis is the general principle of harm: anything that causes severe hardship should be included.
5
Determine the Practical Effect
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): in a famine, Abu Yusuf would consider hoarding fuel or medicine makruh, while Abu Hanifa would not. The mufta bihi is the narrower view of Abu Hanifa.
A mufti may adopt Abu Yusuf's view in extreme circumstances based on necessity (darurah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۳۳] (۳۳) ويكره الاحتكار فى اقوات الآدميين والبهائم اذا كان ذلك في بلد يضرُّ
الى رسول الله الا الله يا عبد الله الم اخبر انک تصوم النهار ... وان لزوجک علیک حقا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب حق الجسم في الصوم ہیں ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۹۷۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیوی کو وطی کا حق ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی اجازت کے بغیر عزل نہ کرے بلکہ اگر شوہر کی خواہش پہلے پوری ہوگئی اور بیوی کی خواہش ابھی پوری نہیں ہوئی ہے تو شوہر بیوی پر برقرار ر ہے۔ اس کا ثبوت حدیث میں ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک ان النبی الله قال اذا غشى الرجل اهله فليصدقها فان قضى حاجته ولم تقض حاجتها فلا يعجلها (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، القول عند الجماع وكيف يضع وفضل الجماع، ج سادس، ص ۱۹۴ نمبر ۱۰۴۶۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شوہر کی خواہش پوری ہو گئی اور بیوی کی خواہش ابھی پوری نہیں ہوئی ہے تو جلدی نہ کرے، ابھی شوہر اس پر ٹھہرا ر ہے۔ اس حدیث سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ خواہش پوری کرنا اس کا حق ہے اس لئے اس کی اجازت کے بغیر عزل نہیں کر سکتا۔
ن بیوی چاہے دوسرے کی باندی ہو پھر بھی اس کا حق آزاد عورت کی طرح ہے۔
[۳۱۳۳] (۳۳) مکروہ ہے آدمیوں اور چوپایوں کی غذا کو روکنا ایسے شہر میں جہاں روکنا اہل شہر کو تکلیف دیتا ہو۔
شہر سے مال خرید خرید کر جمع کرے اور شہر والوں کو اس کی ضرورت کے باوجود ان کو نہ بیچے تا کہ کھانے اور جانور کو کھلانے کی چیز مہنگی ہو جائے ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ آدمی کے کھانے کی چیز یا جانور کے کھانے کی چیز کے علاوہ کو جمع کر کے رکھنا مکروہ ہے یا نہیں اس میں اختلاف
ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مکروہ نہیں اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر شہر والوں کو اس کی سخت ضرورت ہے تو وہ بھی مکروہ ہے۔ حدیث میں احتکار ممنوع ہے۔ ان معمرا قال قال رسول الله الا الله من احتكر فهو خاطی، فقیل لسعید فانک تحتکر ؟ قال سعيد ان معمرا الذي كان يحدث هذا الحديث كان يحتكر (ج) (مسلم شريف، باب تحریم الاحتکار فی الا قوات، ج ۲، ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۱۲۰۵ ار ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی النھی عن الحكرة ، ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۳۴۴۷ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الاحتكار ص ۲۳۵، نمبر ۱۳۶۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ غذا کو روکنا مکروہ ہے۔ آدمی یا جانور کی غذا رو کنا مکروہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ قال ابو داؤد سالت احمد ما الحكرة؟ قال مافيه عيش الناس (و) (ابوداؤد شریف، نمبر ۳۴۴۷) دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ حضرت سعید بن مسیب کھجور کی گٹھلی، بول کی پتی اور بیج کا احتکار کرتے تھے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آدمی کے کھانے اور جانور کے کھانے میں احتکار ہے باقی جن چیزوں کے جمع کرنے میں آدمی اور جانور کو نقصان نہیں ہے اس
حاشیہ : (الف) عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص فرماتے ہیں کہ مجھے حضور نے فرمایا اے عبد اللہ ! مجھے پتا چلا ہے کہ تم دن کو روزہ رکھتے ہو۔ تمہاری بیوی کا تم پر حق ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا بیوی سے جماع کرے تو اچھ طرح کرے۔ پس اگر اپنی حاجت پوری ہو گئی اور اس کی حاجت پوری نہیں ہوئی تو بیوی کو جلدی نہ کرائے بلکہ اس کے اوپر ٹھہرار ہے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا جو مہنگا ہونے کے لئے غلہ رو کے وہ غلطی کر رہا ہے۔ حضرت سعید سے پوچھا آپ کو انکار کرتے ہیں؟ تو حضرت سعید نے فرمایا معمر جو اس حدیث کو نقل کرتے ہیں وہ بھی انکار کرتے تھے (1) حضرت احمد سے پوچھا انکار کیا ہے؟ فرمایا جن غلوں سے لوگ زندگی گزارتے ہیں اس کو مہنگا ہونے
کے لئے روکنا احتکار ہے۔
[3133] (33) It is makruh (disliked) to hoard the foodstuffs of humans and animals when this is in a town and causes harm. ... [3133] (33) It is makruh to withhold the food of humans and animals in a town where it harms the people. A person buys goods from the town and hoards them, and despite the people's need, he does not sell them so that food and fodder become expensive. This is makruh. Whether hoarding things other than human food and animal feed is makruh is subject to disagreement. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not makruh, but Imam Abu Yusuf says that if the townspeople are in dire need, then it is also makruh. The hadith prohibits hoarding: From Ma'mar, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever hoards is a sinner.' It was said to Sa'id: 'You hoard?' He said: 'Ma'mar, who narrated this hadith, also hoarded.' (Muslim, no. 1205; Abu Dawud, no. 3447; Tirmidhi, no. 1367) This shows that hoarding food is makruh. The proof that hoarding human and animal food is makruh is this athar: Abu Dawud said: I asked Ahmad: 'What is hoarding?' He said: 'That upon which people's livelihood depends.' (Abu Dawud, no. 3447) Another narration says that Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab used to hoard date pits, leaves, and seeds, indicating that hoarding human and animal food is included. As for items whose hoarding does not harm humans or animals, it is not makruh. Footnote: (a) ... (b) ... (c) ... (1) ...
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on ihtikar (hoarding). It begins by stating that hoarding foodstuffs for humans and animals in a place where it harms the inhabitants is makruh. The author then explains the scenario: one buys goods from the town and stores them, refusing to sell despite need, causing prices to rise. The ruling is makruh. The passage then addresses a disagreement (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding items other than essential food. Abu Hanifa holds that hoarding non-essential items is not makruh, while Abu Yusuf considers it makruh if the townspeople are in dire need. The proof for the prohibition of hoarding essential items is the hadith that the hoarder is a sinner, and the definition of hoarding from Imam Ahmad: anything upon which people's livelihood depends. The example of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab hoarding date pits and leaves shows that animal feed is included. The passage concludes that items not causing harm to humans or animals are excluded from the prohibition.

Key Terms
احتكار (ihtikar): Hoarding goods, especially foodstuffs, to create artificial scarcity and raise prices.
قوت (qut): Foodstuffs; the basic necessities for humans and animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, is hoarding items other than food for humans and animals (e.g., cloth or hardware) makruh?
A) Yes, it is always makruh.
B) No, it is not makruh.
C) Yes, if the hoarder intends to harm people.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Hoarding essential foodstuffs is makruh tahrimi in Hanafi fiqh; non-essential items are not covered unless causing dire need (per Abu Yusuf).

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling on Hoarding (Ihtikar) – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hoarding with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hoarding food, distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on non-food items, and identify the exceptions for own produce and imported goods.

Core Idea
Hoarding staple foods is makruh when harmful; non-food hoarding is disputed – Abu Hanifa permits, Abu Yusuf prohibits if needed.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri addresses the juristic ruling on ihtikar (hoarding) within the Hanafi school. It first establishes the general rule: hoarding staple foods for humans and animals is makruh when it harms the townspeople. It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding non-food items, supported by hadith and the practice of early scholars. Finally, it clarifies that hoarding one's own produce or imported goods is not considered ihtikar, and the ruler should not fix prices. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for applying the ruling correctly in trade and everyday life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is ihtikar (hoarding) of aqwat (staple foods) for humans and animals. The ruling is makruh (disliked) when two conditions are met: the hoarder buys from the town itself, and the hoarding causes harm to the townspeople.
The harm is typically through price increase and artificial scarcity.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that there is disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding hoarding non-food items (e.g., cloth, fodder). Abu Hanifa holds it is not makruh; Abu Yusuf considers it makruh if the townspeople are in dire need.
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's view is not mentioned here.
3
Analyze the evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith 'Whoever hoards is a sinner' (مَن احتكر فهو خاطئ). This is a zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala hadith, indicating makruh tahrimi. Additionally, the practice of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib hoarding date pits and fodder shows that non-food items are not included in the prohibition.
The term 'khati'' (sinner) implies strong prohibition, but Hanafi usul classifies it as makruh tahrimi due to the zanni evidence.
4
Identify the exceptions
Hoarding one's own produce (ghallat dhi'ati) or goods imported from another town is not considered ihtikar and is not makruh. The condition is that the goods must be bought from the town market for the prohibition to apply.
This is based on the practice of Ibn Tawus and others.
5
Note the additional ruling on price fixing
The passage also states that the ruler (sultan) should not fix prices (tas'ir) arbitrarily, as prices are determined by Allah's decree. However, this is a separate ruling related to market regulation.
This relates to the broader principle of la tas'ir (no price fixing) in Hanafi fiqh.

الاحتكار باهله [۳۱۳۴ (۳۴) ومن احتكر غلّة ضيعته او ما جَلَبَه من بلد آخر فليس
بمحتكر [۳۱۳۵ (۳۵) ولا ينبغى للسلطان ان يُسعر على الناس.
كے احتکار میں کراہیت نہیں ہے۔ اثر یہ ہے۔ قال ابو داؤد و كان سعيد بن المسيب يحتكر النوى والخبط والبزر (الف) (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی النہی عن الحكر ة ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۳۴۴۸) اس اثر میں حضرت سعید بن مسیقب مصلی ، بیول کی پتی اور غلے کی پیج کا احتکار کرتے تھے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ان چیزوں کا احتکار مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ کھانے کا احتکار مکروہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی امامۃ قال نهى رسول الله الله ان يحتكر الطعام (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۴۵ فی احتکار الطعام، ج رابع ص ۳۰۶ نمبر ۰ ۲۰۳۸ راین ماجہ شریف، باب الحكرة والجلب ، ص۳۰۹ نمبر ۲۱۵۵ مصنف عبدالرزاق، ج ثامن، نمبر ۱۴۸۹۶) ون اگر غلہ جمع کرنے میں اہل شہر کو نقصان نہ ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ اور حدیث میں حضرت معمر اس وقت احتکار کرتے جب اس کے جمع کرنے سے لوگوں کو نقصان نہیں ہوتا۔ اقوات : قوۃ کی جمع ہے غذا، البھائم : بھیمۃ کی جمع ہے چوپایا، الاحکار : غلہ کو روک لیتا اور نہ بیچنا۔ [۳۱۳۴] (۳۴) جس نے روک لیا اپنی زمین کا غلہ یاوہ غلہ جو دوسرے شہر سے لایا تو وہ روکنے والا نہیں ہے۔

اپنے شہر سے خرید کر غلہ جمع کرے اور اس کو رو کے تب مکروہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن على قال نھی رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الحكرة بالبلد (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۴۵ فی احتکار الطعام، ج رابع ص ۳۰۷ نمبر ۲۰۳۸۸) اس حديث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اپنے شہر سے خرید کر روکے تو احتکار مکروہ ہے۔ اگر اپنی زمین سے پیداوار کر کے روکے تو اس میں اہل شہر کا حق متعلق نہیں ہوا اس لئے وہ مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن طاؤس عن ابيه قال كان يكون عنده الطعام من ارضه السنتين والثلاث يريد بيعه ينتظر به الغلاء (د) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الحكرة ، ج ثامن، ص ۲۰۲، نمبر ۱۳۸۸۵)

حاشیه : (الف) حضرت سعید بن مسیب محتملی ، بیول کی پتی اور بیج کا احتکار فرماتے تھے (ب) حضور گھانے کے احکار کرنے سے منع فرماتے تھے (ج) حضور شہر میں انکار کرنے سے منع فرماتے تھے (د) ابن طاؤس کے پاس اس کی زمین کا غلہ ہوتا تھا دو سال تک اور تین سال تک۔ اس کو بیچنے کا ارادہ کرتے اور مہنگا ہونے کا انتظار کرتے۔
Hoarding is disliked for food of humans and animals when it harms the people of a town. ... It is disliked to buy goods from the town and store them, not selling despite need, to cause prices to rise. There is a dispute regarding non-food items: Abu Hanifa says it is not disliked, Abu Yusuf says if the townspeople severely need it, it is also disliked. The hadith prohibits hoarding. ...
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of hoarding (ihtikar). It first states the general ruling: hoarding food for humans and animals is makruh (disliked) when it harms the townspeople. The text then clarifies that the hoarding is done by buying from the town itself and withholding. The main point of dispute is whether hoarding non-food items is also makruh. Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is not makruh, while Imam Abu Yusuf considers it makruh if there is severe need. The text provides evidence from hadith, including the hadith 'Whoever hoards is a sinner' and the practice of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib who hoarded date pits and fodder, indicating that only essential foodstuffs are subject to the prohibition. The commentary clarifies that the hadith of Mu'ammar shows that he would hoard only when it did not harm people. Thus, the ruling is specific to situations of harm.

Key Terms
احتكار (ihtikar): Hoarding goods, specifically buying from the market and withholding to cause price rise and harm to the people.
أقوات (aqwat): Plural of qut: staple food grains that sustain life, such as wheat, barley, dates.
البهائم (al-baha'im): Plural of bahimah: domestic animals, livestock whose feed is included in the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, is hoarding a commodity like cloth (not food) makruh?
A) Yes, all hoarding is makruh.
B) No, it is not makruh unless it severely harms the people.
C) Yes, but only if cloth is a necessity.
D) No, it is halal unconditionally.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on ihtikar is nuanced: food hoarding is makruh if harmful, non-food hoarding is disputed, and own produce/imports are exempt.
